" data-portal-copyright= " John Kenney " **28;16673;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1760773 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;16703;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; Montreal is stepping up its measurers to help homeless people cope with the coronavirus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; They include opening five outdoor day centres , expanding shelter room for men and women , and adding temporary public toilets .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We&amp;rsquo ; re working with our partners to ensure the homeless have access to facilities that allow them to practise good hygiene while respecting the protocol established to deal with the virus , &amp;rdquo ; said Rosannie Filato , the Montreal executive committee member responsible for public safety .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The first two day centres opened this weekend at Cabot Square and Place &amp;Eacute ; milie-Gamelin .
Three others will open shortly .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Filato said it was important to get these centres opened because indoor day centres had to shut down to respect the ban on large gatherings .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We had to find room outdoors , which allowed us to serve this vulnerable population , but also offered enough space that we could respect social distancing , &amp;rdquo ; Filato said .
&amp;ldquo ; There will be facilities to wash and the homeless will be able to something good to eat .
People will be able to get information about the virus and what they can do to protect themselves .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;img src= " https : **33;16739;TOOLONG .
title= " Nelson Norville and Rose Lavan sit under a shelter provided by the city of Montreal at Cabot Square in Montreal on Saturday , March 28 , 2020 .
This was the first day of a day centre set up to respond to the COVID-19 crisis with the homeless population .
" alt= " Nelson Norville and Rose Lavan sit under a shelter provided by the city of Montreal at Cabot Square in Montreal on Saturday , March 28 , 2020 .
This was the first day of a day centre set up to respond to the COVID-19 crisis with the homeless population .
" data-portal-copyright= " John Kenney " **28;16774;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1760775 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; The city&amp;rsquo ; s health department will manage the Cabot Square centre along with Resilience Montreal , which has experience dealing with homeless people , particularly among the Indigenous population .
There&amp;rsquo ; s also help from the province , community organizations and volunteers .
The Red Cross was on hand to help get things rolling during the weekend .
Filato said the five centres will be able to accommodate 1,000 people on a daily basis .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The former Royal Victoria Hospital site on Pins Ave .
has been used as an emergency shelter , but it will now be reserved for patients who require isolation .
There is a shelter for women at the YMCA on Stanley St .
and for men at Complexe Guy-Favreau .
The city&amp;rsquo ; s website says new locations will be available soon .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The city is also installing 24 portable washrooms , mostly in the downtown area .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; This is important because many of these people relied on restaurants that are now closed , &amp;rdquo ; Filato said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The city ramped up its efforts to curb the spread of the coronavirus when Mayor Val&amp;eacute ; rie Plante declared a health emergency on Friday .
Among the new regulations are a ban on dogs in city parks and a limit on joggers who are required to stay within one kilometre of their homes .

NewsFitness : Become a runner in eight weekshttp : **35;17121;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;17158;TOOLONG .
title= " The Couch to 5K program gives your body plenty of time to get used to pounding the pavement .
It starts with lots of walking , but before you know it you 're running 30 minutes , which is about five kilometres .
" alt= " The Couch to 5K program gives your body plenty of time to get used to pounding the pavement .
It starts with lots of walking , but before you know it you 're running 30 minutes , which is about five kilometres .
" data-portal-copyright= " Allen McInnis " **28;17193;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1756563 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;17223;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; Combine the current need for solo exercise and the arrival of spring , and it&amp;rsquo ; s the perfect time for a Couch to 5K running program .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Created a decade ago , the eight-week program has successfully turned hundreds of walkers into runners .
That said , the workouts aren&amp;rsquo ; t limited to folks who want to run .
They also work for walkers who want to put a little extra pep in their step .
Just substitute the running intervals with brisk walking and you&amp;rsquo ; re good to go .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The beauty of this program is that it allows for a gradual introduction to running , giving your body plenty of time to get used to pounding the pavement .
It starts with lots of walking and small bursts of running .
As the weeks go by , the walking is replaced by running .
Before you know it , you&amp;rsquo ; re running 30 minutes , which is about five kilometres ( give or take ) .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Another plus of the Couch to 5K program is that it takes just 30 minutes ( plus or minus a couple minutes here and there ) three days a week .
I suggest you take a day off between training sessions , but if you need to do a couple back to back or put more than a couple of days between workouts , no problem .
Just make sure you do all the workouts &amp;mdash ; don&amp;rsquo ; t skip ahead , as the program is meant to introduce running gradually and gently .
That includes non-runners who are already in good shape .
No matter how fit you are aerobically , your musculoskeletal system needs time to adjust to the impact stress of running , so patience is your friend .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Don&amp;rsquo ; t worry about how fast you&amp;rsquo ; re moving .
You need to find a pace you can sustain for the whole running interval .
Those first few short intervals seem pretty doable , but as you get closer to running three uninterrupted minutes it starts to feel more challenging .
So find a comfortable pace and stay there .
The rule of thumb in running is distance before speed .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Before you get started , make sure you have a good pair of running shoes .
You also need a basic kit of athletic wear , which should be made of breathable fabric that moves with you and has no rough seams .
And ladies , make sure you have a good sports bra .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Finally , feel free to check in with any questions .
I&amp;rsquo ; ll answer as many as possible and publish some of the best at the bottom of my weekly column .
You can also share your successes and struggles .
If we&amp;rsquo ; ve learned one thing these past few weeks , it&amp;rsquo ; s that we&amp;rsquo ; re one large community , so stay calm and run on ! &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;17259;TOOLONG .

minutes ) &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;nbsp ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Session 2&lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Walk 15 minutes &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Run 5 minutes &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Walk 10 minutes &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Find a hill during your walk .
Run up and walk down x 2 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; ( 30 minutes ) &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;nbsp ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Session 3&lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Walk 5 minutes &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; ( Run 3 minutes / Walk 1 minute ) x 5 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Walk 5 minutes &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; ( 30 minutes ) &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;nbsp ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;Week 6&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Session 1&lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Walk 4 minutes &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; ( Run 8 minutes / Walk 30 seconds ) x 3 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; ( 29 .

&lt;/p&gt; Jill Barker , Special to Montreal GazetteSun , 29 Mar 2020 13:23:19 **45;17654;TOOLONG &amp;amp ; FitnessHealthLifeSeniors isolated by the coronavirus crisis embrace balcony Zumba classhttp : **35;17701;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;17738;TOOLONG .
title= " Seniors participate in an outdoor Zumba class from the balcony of a seniors ' residence in Blainville on Friday March 27 , 2020 .
" alt= " Seniors participate in an outdoor Zumba class from the balcony of a seniors ' residence in Blainville on Friday March 27 , 2020 .
" data-portal-copyright= " Pierre Obendrauf " **28;17773;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1760365 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;17803;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; BLAINVILLE &amp;mdash ; A Zumba instructor who goes by the name H&amp;eacute ; l&amp;egrave ; ne Antidote provided some joy for a group of seniors at the R&amp;eacute ; sidence Le Nobilis on Friday .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The residents , who have been isolated in their apartments because of the coronavirus , flocked to their balconies to be led through a series of exercises led&amp;nbsp ; by Antidote , whose brightly coloured outfit wouldn&amp;rsquo ; t have been out of place at a Cirque du Soleil show .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It was really great , &amp;rdquo ; said Ophelia Roy .
&amp;ldquo ; When they gave us our rainbows ( signs with a rainbow motif and the word &amp;ldquo ; &amp;ccedil ; a va bien aller&amp;rdquo ; ) , it really touched me .
It&amp;rsquo ; s very nice .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Roy said it was good to feel a sense of community with her fellow residents even though it was limited to greetings exchanged at a distance .
She noted social distancing is taken very seriously at the independent living complex .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;img src= " https : **33;17839;TOOLONG .
title= " Ophelia Roy participates in a seniors outdoor Zumba class from the balcony of the seniors residence in Blainville on Friday March 27 , 2020 .
" alt= " Ophelia Roy participates in a seniors outdoor Zumba class from the balcony of the seniors residence in Blainville on Friday March 27 , 2020 .
" data-portal-copyright= " Pierre Obendrauf " **28;17874;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1760590 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We don&amp;rsquo ; t see each other , &amp;rdquo ; explained Roy .
&amp;ldquo ; We&amp;rsquo ; re not allowed to visit .
We mostly go out on our balconies .
We can talk to each other , but this is the first time I see people walking around outside .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Roy and her fellow residents are aware of the importance of exercise and she said she has been heeding her children&amp;rsquo ; s advice and getting outside to walk in addition to doing some exercises in her apartment .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; I try to to keep busy because usually we have a lot of activities here , but they&amp;rsquo ; ve been cancelled , &amp;rdquo ; Roy said .
&amp;ldquo ; Zumba , I do every week .
&amp;rdquo ; The residence has an indoor swimming pool and an exercise room , but both have been closed by government decree .
An onsite caf&amp;eacute ; and hair salon are also shuttered and the isolation extends to a ban on visitors .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s scary , but what can we do , nothing , &amp;rdquo ; Roy said when asked about the pandemic .
&amp;ldquo ; I&amp;rsquo ; m very disappointed that people are not listening .
If everyone had stayed home , we would be okay .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Armande Beauvais was also among the participants in Friday&amp;rsquo ; s class and , while she enjoyed the lesson , she had one minor complaint .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It was fun , but it was rather cold on this side of the building because the sun isn&amp;rsquo ; t here yet , &amp;rdquo ; Beauvais said .
Her apartment is on the north side of the building and the balconies are in the shade in early afternoon .
Roy&amp;rsquo ; s apartment is on the south side and she and neighbours were treated to sunshine for their class .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Beauvais said the order to isolate has forced her to change her exercise routine .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We can&amp;rsquo ; t exercise as a group , but I try to do some exercises in my apartment , even if it&amp;rsquo ; s not very large , and I try to come and walk outside every day , especially when the weather is good , &amp;rdquo ; Beauvais said .
&amp;ldquo ; If not , I walk through the halls .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; This was good and we&amp;rsquo ; re also expecting to go outside on our balconies and sing but , when it&amp;rsquo ; s cold , it&amp;rsquo ; s&amp;rsquo ; not easy , &amp;rdquo ; Beauvais said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The important thing , Beauvais said , is she&amp;rsquo ; s healthy and she&amp;rsquo ; s trying to stay healthy .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; I&amp;rsquo ; m 81 and , thank God , it&amp;rsquo ; s not too bad .

&lt;/p&gt; Pat Hickey , Montreal GazetteFri , 27 Mar 2020 22:44:11 **45;18386;TOOLONG &amp;amp ; FitnessHealthLocal NewsSeniorsCoronavirus : Montreal family doctors turn to telemedicine for most patientshttp : **32;18433;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;18467;TOOLONG .
title= " " The patients are extremely happy because they do n't want to risk catching the virus coming in to get a renewal of their blood pressure medications , " says Dr .
Mark Roper , director of the Queen Elizabeth super clinic .
" alt= " " The patients are extremely happy because they do n't want to risk catching the virus coming in to get a renewal of their blood pressure medications , " says Dr .
Mark Roper , director of the Queen Elizabeth super clinic .
" data-portal-copyright= " Photo courtesy of Mark Roper " **28;18502;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1757042 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;18532;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; Family doctors across Montreal have switched to telemedicine to examine as many as 90 per cent of their patients&amp;nbsp ; &amp;mdash ; a new development that is likely to influence the way physicians practise even after the &lt;a href= " https : **33;18568;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;COVID-19&lt;/a&gt; pandemic ends .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Patients with abdominal pain and other serious conditions are still being examined in doctors&amp;rsquo ; offices .
But in most cases , doctors , nurses , dietitians and social workers are relying on the phone , and to a lesser extent video calls , to communicate with patients .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; For years , telemedicine has languished in Quebec , except in the Far North where doctors have used it routinely .
But since the World Health Organization declared COVID-19 to be a pandemic on March 11 , the practice is now being embraced by family doctors across the province .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Telemedicine is coming into its own for family medicine groups , &amp;rdquo ; &lt;a href= " https : **33;18603;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Dr .
Mark Roper&lt;/a&gt; , director of the Queen Elizabeth super clinic on Marlowe Ave .
, told the Montreal Gazette on Tuesday .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s working very well .
We&amp;rsquo ; re sparing patients from having to go outside and be exposed to people on the m&amp;eacute ; tro and on the bus .
We&amp;rsquo ; re sparing people in the waiting room from ( potentially ) picking up ( the coronavirus ) .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Telemedicine is still a patchwork of different systems in Quebec .
But the need to maintain social distancing is driving doctors in clinics to work more closely with systems like the &lt;a href= " https : **33;18638;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Dossier sant ? Qu ? bec&lt;/a&gt; , the provincial network of electronic medical records ; and &lt;span class= " st " &gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;18673;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Rendez-vous sant ? Qu ? bec&lt;/a&gt; , which lets people book appointments at clinics online .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The last incentive to switch over came when the R&amp;eacute ; gie de l&amp;rsquo ; assurance maladie du Qu&amp;eacute ; bec added a new billing code two weeks ago allowing doctors to invoice the medicare board for a telehealth consultation .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Being in a wartime situation , technology advances very quickly , and the electronic medical record providers are adding the video conferencing very quickly now , &amp;rdquo ; Roper explained .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Before the pandemic , the Queen Elizabeth clinic did not rely at all on telemedicine .
Today , it&amp;rsquo ; s using it for more than 90 per cent of its patients .
By comparison , doctors are treating no more than 50 patients a day at the clinic in **26;18708;TOOLONG ; ce , down from the usual 150 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;img src= " https : **33;18736;TOOLONG .
title= " " The patients are extremely happy because they do n't want to risk catching the virus coming in to get a renewal of their blood pressure medications , " says Dr .
Mark Roper , director of the Queen Elizabeth super clinic .
" alt= " " The patients are extremely happy because they do n't want to risk catching the virus coming in to get a renewal of their blood pressure medications , " says Dr .
Mark Roper , director of the Queen Elizabeth super clinic .
" data-portal-copyright= " Photo courtesy of Mark Roper " **28;18771;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1757042 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; All scheduled appointments for the next two weeks are being converted to telemedicine consultations .
Doctors and nurses will speak to patients over the phone , or ask them to upload an app on their phone for a secure video call .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We had a lady with swollen legs due to heart failure and we wanted to see if her legs were improving , &amp;rdquo ; Roper recalled .
&amp;ldquo ; She couldn&amp;rsquo ; t talk very well .
She&amp;rsquo ; s quite elderly .
So her daughter turned her iPhone camera to her mother&amp;rsquo ; s legs and we had a look at the legs , and then we saw that they were less swollen than before .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Following a telemedicine consultation , doctors will send faxes for drug prescriptions to the pharmacy .
They can refer patients to a specialist by faxing a referral to the doctor or using a computerized referral system to choose the earliest available specialist .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Some patients still have to show up at the clinic to get a bacterial culture done , to have their blood drawn or to take a urine test , but in such cases a dedicated team is on site to process the samples quickly .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The patients are extremely happy because they don&amp;rsquo ; t want to risk catching the virus coming in to get a renewal of their blood pressure medications , &amp;rdquo ; Roper said .
&amp;ldquo ; If they need to go to the emergency , obviously we call the ER ahead and tell them this patient is coming in and we send a summary .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; More than 30,000 patients depend on the Queen E clinic .
But what about the tens of thousands in Montreal who don&amp;rsquo ; t have a family doctor ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; For such patients , Roper recommended &lt;span class= " st " &gt;Rendez-vous sant ? Qu ? bec ( RVSQ ) &lt;/span&gt; , known in English as the &lt;a href= " https : **33;18801;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Quebec Medical Appointment Scheduler&lt;/a&gt; .
Patients can book an appointment through the website with a clinic that&amp;rsquo ; s closest to where they live .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Before COVID-19 , appointments filled up quickly each morning , or were simply not available .
But with most clinics now filled to half capacity , that should not pose a problem .
At the Queen E clinic , patients booking through RVSQ are seen either the same day or the following day .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " **28;18836;TOOLONG " target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **35;18866;TOOLONG &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " http : **25;18903;TOOLONG " target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **31;18930;TOOLONG .

NewsNewsChristopher Labos : Blood pressure medication , ibuprofen and COVID-19http : **32;19419;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;19453;TOOLONG .
title= " A physician takes a patient 's blood pressure .
" People are understandably concerned about COVID-19 and , unfortunately , in this climate of uncertainty , preliminary studies are often given much more credence than they deserve , " Christopher Labos writes .
" alt= " A physician takes a patient 's blood pressure .
" People are understandably concerned about COVID-19 and , unfortunately , in this climate of uncertainty , preliminary studies are often given much more credence than they deserve , " Christopher Labos writes .
" data-portal-copyright= " Bill Keay " **28;19488;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1756262 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **33;19518;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; In the past week , there were reports that some common medications might make COVID-19 worse .
Many news reports stated that anti-inflammatories like ibuprofen and a class of common blood pressure medications might either make infection more likely or the illness more severe .
While the World Health Organization initially put out a press release suggesting that people might want to avoid ibuprofen during the current outbreak , it subsequently &lt;a href= " https : **33;19553;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;withdrew that statement&lt;/a&gt; citing insufficient evidence .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The blood pressure medication story began with a &lt;a href= " https : **33;19588;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;research letter&lt;/a&gt; published in the journal Lancet Respiratory Medicine .
It asked , rather provocatively , if patients with hypertension and diabetes were at increased risk of COVID-19 infection .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; There is little doubt that patients with pre-existing medical conditions are at higher risk if they become infected .
Of course , patients with high blood pressure and diabetes are more likely to be older , and age in and of itself would increase that risk , as well .
It is , however , another thing entirely to claim that high blood pressure and diabetes make it more likely that you will catch the virus in the first place .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The hypothesis centred on the fact that this current coronavirus binds and infects cells using an enzyme called ACE2 .
Higher levels of ACE2 would , in theory , make it more likely for the virus to infect the cells of the lungs where this enzyme is produced .
Therefore , any medications that increase ACE2 levels could potentially increase the risk of infection .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; By rather unfortunate coincidence , many common blood pressure medications can increase ACE2 levels .
The research letter noted that medications like ibuprofen , as well as blood pressure pills like ACE inhibitors and ARBs , can increase ACE2 levels and should be monitored during the current pandemic .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The implications of this recommendation were profound .
ACE inhibitors ( like ramipril/altace and peridopril/coversyl ) and ARBs ( like valsartan/diovan and irbesartan/avapro ) are used not just to treat blood pressure , but also to protect the kidneys in patients with diabetes and to help cardiac function in patients with heart failure .
It would not be going too far to state that they are a cornerstone of treatment , and stopping them in light of the COVID-19 pandemic would almost certainly be disastrous for patients .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The danger , as was &lt;a href= " https : **32;19623;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;pointed out&lt;/a&gt; by numerous cardiovascular groups and societies , is that if patients were to suddenly stop these medications , it could lead to rapid spikes in high blood pressure , which could in turn lead to strokes , heart attacks and acute episodes of heart failure .
When it comes to cardiovascular care in stable patients , there is something to be said for not rocking the boat .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The &lt;a href= " https : **33;19657;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;recommendation to avoid ibuprofen&lt;/a&gt; is a little bit different .
While there are some people who rely on anti-inflammatories to treat conditions like arthritis , they are not generally recommended for most people because of their side effects .
Anti-inflammatories like these can raise your blood pressure , cause stomach ulcers and affect your kidneys in high doses .
While probably not harmful if taken sparingly in small doses , most physicians , myself included , would probably recommend that patients start with acetaminophen ( Tylenol ) if trying to treat a fever or mild aches and pains .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; I myself am somewhat unconvinced that any of these medications is really having any significant effect on the spread of COVID-19 .
People are understandably concerned about COVID-19 and , unfortunately , in this climate of uncertainty , preliminary studies are often given much more credence than they deserve .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; So while I might recommend that people avoid ibuprofen anyway , given its side effects that have nothing to do with virology , suddenly stopping your cardiac medication would be a catastrophically bad idea that could land many people in hospital .
And we can ill afford that right now .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;em&gt;Christopher Labos&lt;/em&gt; &lt;em&gt; is a Montreal doctor and an associate with the McGill Office for Science and Society .
He also co-hosts a podcast called The Body of Evidence .
&lt;/em&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;19692;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;19734;TOOLONG .
columns by Christopher **26;19769;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;19797;TOOLONG .
all our coverage on the **32;19832;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Note to readers : &lt;/strong&gt; &amp;nbsp ; We know the speed and volume of coronavirus-related news is overwhelming and a little frightening .
To help with that , we will dedicate a Montreal Gazette reporter each day to devote their time to synthesizing the most important coronavirus-related news , especially as it relates to life in Montreal and Quebec .

target= " blank " class= " c-link " rel= " noopener " &gt;Follow their updates on March 24 right here&lt;/a&gt; .
All our coronavirus-related news can always be found here : &amp;nbsp ; &lt;a href= " http : **34;19902;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " class= " c-link " rel= " noopener " **31;19938;TOOLONG .
&lt;br&gt; Sign up for our new email newsletter dedicated to local coronavirus coverage here : &amp;nbsp ; &lt;a href= " http : **34;19971;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " class= " c-link " rel= " noopener " **31;20007;TOOLONG .
&lt;/p&gt; Christopher Labos , Special to Montreal GazetteTue , 24 Mar 2020 22:01:18 **45;20040;TOOLONG .
Do active parents raise active kids ? http : **35;20087;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;20124;TOOLONG .
title= " Former U .
First Lady Michelle Obama dances with school children during a debut of a school exercise program Feb .
28 , 2013 in Chicago .
" alt= " Former U .
First Lady Michelle Obama dances with school children during a debut of a school exercise program Feb .
28 , 2013 in Chicago .
" data-portal-copyright= " Tasos Katopodis " **28;20159;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1747990 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; Are active parents more likely to raise active children than parents who never work up a sweat ? And does a failure to engage your children in an active lifestyle mean they&amp;rsquo ; ll grow up spending more time in front of a screen than in the playground or kicking a soccer ball ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The Canadian Physical Activity Guidelines recommends preschoolers accumulate at least 180 minutes of physical activity spread throughout the day and progress toward at least 60 minutes of energetic play by the age of five .
From the ages of five to 11 , the guidelines suggest children accumulate at least 60 minutes of moderate to vigorous intensity physical activity daily .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Those are ambitious targets for kids to accomplish on their own , which implies that parents have a role in encouraging their children to be physically active .
That responsibility doesn&amp;rsquo ; t just involve providing opportunities for kids to be active , but also by limiting sedentary activities and modelling their own active lifestyle .
After all , kids learn not just by doing but also by observing .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Yet despite the importance of an active lifestyle , little is known about the ABCs of raising an active child including whether children are more likely to accumulate the majority of their active minutes in school/ daycare or in the presence of their parents .
Some studies suggest that young children are more active under the care of others than they are at home .
In fact , only a small percentage of daily physical activity accumulated by kids and their parents is accrued together .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; To get a better sense of the number of minutes per day children and their parents are active both individually and together , a research team from California State University at Fullerton put accelerometers on 26 parent-and-child ( two to six years age ) teams for 10 days .
They also requested parents fill out a daily online diary reporting the amount of time their child spent with their parents and any other caregivers like babysitters and teachers .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The results showed that when parents and children were together , the parent&amp;rsquo ; s activity , or lack thereof , directly influenced their child .
The more active the parent , the more active the child .
A similar dynamic was found for sedentary behaviour ; when together , children modelled the behaviour of their inactive parents .
This association may seem obvious , but studies suggest that parents and children spend only a small amount of time being active together .
Indeed , most active parents work out without their child in tow , going to the gym or out for a bike ride or run solo instead of as a family unit .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The results from this study do not support the notion that active parents will yield active children by merely being active themselves , &amp;rdquo ; the researchers said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The other important revelation by the researchers is that within the family dynamic , not all physical activity need be initiated by the parents .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; An active child may require the parent to be active to keep up with the child , &amp;rdquo ; the researchers said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Frankly , it doesn&amp;rsquo ; t matter who motivates whom , but it&amp;rsquo ; s clear that parents and children need to spend more time being active together .
Visits to the park should involve running , jumping , sliding , climbing and swinging alongside children instead of watching from a park bench .
And it&amp;rsquo ; s never too early to practise the building blocks of physical activity , including changes in speed and direction of movement and other sports-related actions like throwing , catching and kicking .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;20189;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : //wp .
" &gt;Fitness : Do you have what it takes to be an ultra-marathoner ? &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : //wp .
" &gt;Fitness : It 's never too soon to embrace positive **26;20231;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : //wp .
" &gt;Fitness : Treat those aching knees and hips with **29;20259;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;p&gt; The goal is to ensure children accumulate the recommended minutes of daily vigorous activity associated with their age .
It&amp;rsquo ; s also important that children see their parents enjoying themselves while being active .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; A word of caution , however : Kids don&amp;rsquo ; t exercise like adults .
Unlike the adult tendency to get in as many minutes of exercise as possible in one session , children are more comfortable being active in short bursts .
Kids naturally gravitate toward interval workouts , interspersed with generous bouts of rest or light-intensity activity .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The idea of making exercise a family affair is particularly important as children tend to move less the older they get .
Active play is replaced with more sedentary pastimes and exercise tends to be scheduled versus spontaneous .
Families that make physical activity part of their lifestyle are more likely to continue the trend as the children get older .
Active vacations , weekends spent skiing , tobogganing , skating , paddling , hiking or exploring new activities like zip lining and indoor rock climbing are all activities kids and parents can enjoy together .
Active parents only raise active kids if the whole family learns to love exercise together , instead of parents prioritizing their own exercise goals .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; This supports the notion that active parents must be active around their child to provide valuable behaviour modelling , while being active not in the presence of the child may not provide the same opportunity for such modelling to occur , &amp;rdquo ; said the research team from the University of California Fullerton .
&lt;/p&gt; Jill Barker , Special to Montreal GazetteSun , 22 Mar 2020 13:00:35 **45;20290;TOOLONG .
NewsCoronavirus : Staying home can save lives , physician pleadshttp : **34;20337;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;20373;TOOLONG .
title= " Stay at home , urges Dr .
Giada Sebastiani , who is an associate professor of medicine at McGill University " alt= " Stay at home , urges Dr .
Giada Sebastiani , who is an associate professor of medicine at McGill University " data-portal-copyright= " Handout " **28;20408;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1750282 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;20438;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; Stay home .
Save lives .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Dr .
Giada Sebastiani speaks as a physician , an associate professor of medicine at McGill University and a mother when she implores parents to stay at home with their children .
No play dates .
No parties .
No outings .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; In an attempt to contain the spread of the COVID-19 pandemic sweeping the globe , &lt;a href= " https : **33;20474;TOOLONG .
Fran ? ois Legault last week ordered the province 's schools , universities and daycares closed for two weeks&lt;/a&gt; .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; This is not a vacation .
The government of Quebec is in emergency mode , &amp;rdquo ; Sebastiani said on Tuesday .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Provincial health authorities announced 74 confirmed cases of COVID-19 late Tuesday , up from 50 on Monday .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;img src= " https : **33;20509;TOOLONG .
title= " " alt= " " data-portal-copyright= " " **28;20544;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; Around the world there have been nearly 200,000 documented cases of the influenza-like respiratory illness since it was first detected in December in China , and almost 8,000 deaths .
Although many cases are mild , the elderly and those with underlying health conditions are especially vulnerable .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It is very important for families to understand that they can have an important , active role in this phase of the epidemic , &amp;rdquo ; Sebastiani said .
&amp;ldquo ; They can help the physicians and other health care professionals in saving lives &amp;mdash ; just by staying home .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We have a small window of opportunity to avoid the exponential phase of the outbreak : one week , a few days &amp;mdash ; not more .
We must take advantage of it .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Hospitals are reducing non-urgent visits and procedures to be prepared for a flood of COVID-19 cases , Sebastiani wrote in a Facebook community group post .
She urged parents to &amp;ldquo ; please help us flatten the curve , &amp;rdquo ; to slow the spread of the virus so that fewer people need to seek treatment at any given time , &amp;ldquo ; so that we can be ready to face upcoming emergencies .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Children who contract COVID-19 are often asymptomatic .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; If we start saying it&amp;rsquo ; s OK for the children go to the park with their grandparents or to share play dates or share common spaces , this will lead to a propagation of this illness , &amp;rdquo ; she said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Families can do so much by promoting the &lt;a href= " https : **33;20574;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;social distancing&lt;/a&gt; the government of Quebec has communicated so well .
I think the government has taken very important steps &amp;ndash ; and much more quickly than what happened in some European countries , where the epidemic went out of control .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Sebastiani , who is a liver specialist at the McGill University Health Centre , emphasized that she was sharing her personal view , as a physician and a mother of two .
She is also speaking as an Italian : Italy is the country with the worst COVID-19 outbreak outside China .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;img src= " https : **33;20609;TOOLONG .
title= " Stay at home , urges Dr .
Giada Sebastiani , who is an associate professor of medicine at McGill University " alt= " Stay at home , urges Dr .
Giada Sebastiani , who is an associate professor of medicine at McGill University " data-portal-copyright= " Handout " **28;20644;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1750282 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; I know exactly how the virus can put the health care system of a country on the verge of collapse .
I am from Venice : All my family and friends are there , &amp;rdquo ; she said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; In Italy , when the schools closed , there were all these children out in the parks with their grandparents , socializing with others .
There was no clear message , unfortunately , to stay home .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; On Feb .
21 there were 14 cases of COVID-19 in Lombardy in northwest Italy , where the first outbreaks were detected .
By Tuesday Italy had more than 31,500 cases .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We want people to stay at home and minimize all social contacts , &amp;rdquo ; said Dr .
Eric Litvak , medical chief , infectious disease prevention and control , with Montreal&amp;rsquo ; s Public Health Department on Tuesday .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Provided that they do this , they are continuing to press the brake on the pandemic , &amp;rdquo ; he said .
&amp;ldquo ; We are in a car and the virus is pushing on the gas pedal .
We are sitting next to the virus with no control over the gas pedal .
But we have control over the brake .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; That is why all the measures are in place .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " **30;20674;TOOLONG " target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **37;20706;TOOLONG &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;20745;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;20787;TOOLONG .

NewsNewsDoctors cut down on non-essential care to prep for coronavirus fighthttp : **35;21227;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;21264;TOOLONG .
title= " A sign outlines precautions to be taken entering a room designated to treat potential COVID-19 patients at Montreal 's Jewish General Hospital .
" alt= " A sign outlines precautions to be taken entering a room designated to treat potential COVID-19 patients at Montreal 's Jewish General Hospital .
" data-portal-copyright= " Allen McInnis " **28;21299;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1748371 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;21329;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; As an infectious diseases specialist and medical microbiologist , Marty Teltscher is one of the doctors at the Jewish General Hospital dealing with patients who have contracted COVID-19 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Teltscher works as a consulting physician for those treating patients infected by the novel coronavirus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The biggest part of his job now is working with the team of infectious diseases doctors to pare down how many regular patients they are treating , both so they can be available to help treat COVID-19 patients , and to reduce the number of people in the hospital , in order to reduce the chance of spreading an infection .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Today in our walk-in clinic , where we usually see up to 35 people , we have seen eight , &amp;rdquo ; Teltscher said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Although he has reduced the number of patients he treats daily , Teltscher said the virus is keeping him and his team very busy , &amp;ldquo ; reorganizing in order to prioritize certain services and equipment .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; While most doctors in the hospital aren&amp;rsquo ; t dealing with patients who are infected , Teltscher said all hospital personnel are now pulling together to get ready for an influx of COVID-19 patients .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; What we&amp;rsquo ; re expecting is the potential for many people to need medical support and a significant number of people who will need critical care and equipment , &amp;rdquo ; Teltscher said .
&amp;ldquo ; That&amp;rsquo ; s what happened in Italy , and you end up depleting supplies and personnel , and then you are left with a system that can&amp;rsquo ; t cope even with people who are not infected .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We know what this virus can do is completely disrupt the healthcare system by overloading it in a rapid fashion .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Teltscher said he&amp;rsquo ; s not afraid to be working with COVID-19 patients , but he is concerned about what lies ahead .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s challenging , and to a certain degree frustrating , &amp;rdquo ; he said .
&amp;ldquo ; I wouldn&amp;rsquo ; t say this is an interesting time I&amp;rsquo ; d like to study .
I&amp;rsquo ; d rather not be here at all .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Michael Sidel is a neurologist who sees stroke patients in the hospital .
And while he doesn&amp;rsquo ; t deal directly with COVID-19 patients , his whole practice is affected by the virus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Sidel , an associate professor of neurology and neurosurgery at McGill , said the clinics where he works are paring down the number of patients they see in the hospital , to do as much follow-up on the phone and work from home if possible .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; He too is working with a team of neurologists who will decide in the coming days which services they must offer and which ones can be put on hold to reduce the number of people in the hospital so that more resources can be made available for the fight against COVID-19 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Unless they are critically urgent , we&amp;rsquo ; re trying not to see people in the hospital , &amp;rdquo ; Sidel said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The ward where Sidel works is now being converted into the area in the hospital to treat patients infected with the coronavirus .
As such , many of the nurses he has worked with have been retrained in recent weeks to deal with the pandemic .
He said he is impressed by the dedication of the nursing staff to work on patients infected with this virus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The nurses on the ward are stressed .
Nobody really knows what will happen , &amp;rdquo ; he said .
&amp;ldquo ; That hangs over everything .
There is a tremendous sense of work and dedication , and altruism .
Anyone working on the front lines , there&amp;rsquo ; s a measure of self-sacrifice there .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; He said he&amp;rsquo ; s not concerned he will be infected , even though he works with nurses that come in contact with the virus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; At a certain point , you have to trust that the measures being taken are protecting the healthcare workers and the people that they come in contact with , so I&amp;rsquo ; m protected and my family is protected .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;img src= " https : **33;21365;TOOLONG .
title= " ER doctor Mitch Shulman .
" alt= " ER doctor Mitch Shulman .
" data-portal-copyright= " Pierre Obendrauf " **28;21400;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1197688 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; As an emergency room doctor at the McGill University Health Centre , Mitch Shulman would normally be on the front lines working with infected patients .
However , he recently returned from a trip abroad and will have to isolate himself for two weeks on the orders of Quebec Premier Fran&amp;ccedil ; ois Legault .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Although he knows the precaution is a sensible one , it will be difficult for him to be sitting on the sidelines knowing his colleagues covering his shifts will have their hands full .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The procedure for dealing with patients who may be infected or are infected is very labour intensive , in terms of the donning of gear , &amp;rdquo ; he said .
&amp;ldquo ; You have to be meticulous about the protocol and if you&amp;rsquo ; re in the gear , it&amp;rsquo ; s really tough to breathe .
It&amp;rsquo ; s tough to maintain focus and concentration for many hours at a stretch , especially if you&amp;rsquo ; re gowning and regowning .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; There are a lot of logistical concerns , along with the practical one , like : &amp;lsquo ; am I going to get infected and bring the virus home ? ' &amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Teltscher said while healthcare workers are doing their part , he believes everyone in the country has a role to play .
The outcome will depend on how well average citizens heed the warnings to avoid social gatherings and reduce contact with others as much as possible .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s the most important group effort that we have seen , probably in our lifetime , &amp;rdquo ; he said .
&amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s as important as if we would be going to war .
Everybody has to contribute in all aspects of society if we&amp;rsquo ; re going to succeed .

NewsBrownstein : Montreal businesses among many singing coronavirus blueshttp : **35;22081;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;22118;TOOLONG .
title= " Shoppers and a renovation work crew are shown at Fairview shopping mall in Pointe-Claire at lunchtime on Monday , March 16 , 2020 .
" alt= " Shoppers and a renovation work crew are shown at Fairview shopping mall in Pointe-Claire at lunchtime on Monday , March 16 , 2020 .
" data-portal-copyright= " Peter McCabe " **28;22153;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1748349 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;22183;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; No easy task , but I found some tourists strolling Ste-Catherine St .
Jacky Le Naour , his wife Fran&amp;ccedil ; oise , their son and daughter-in-law had just arrived from France&amp;rsquo ; s Brittany region a few days earlier .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s great , almost like we have the whole city to ourselves , &amp;rdquo ; Jacky said .
&amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s our first time here and we are managing to enjoy ourselves , even with so many places closed .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The family is well aware of the coronavirus , having dealt with it in France .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We&amp;rsquo ; ve been lucky so far , &amp;rdquo ; interjected the smiling Fran&amp;ccedil ; oise .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Lucky that they arrived before quarantine and strict isolation policies took hold here .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Suffice it to say , these are trying times for the city&amp;rsquo ; s tourism trade .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;img src= " https : **33;22219;TOOLONG .
title= " Andrew Torriani , President and CEO of Ritz Carleton Montreal .
" alt= " Andrew Torriani , President and CEO of Ritz Carleton Montreal .
" data-portal-copyright= " Vincenzo D'Alto " **28;22254;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1748338 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Very challenging days , &amp;rdquo ; Ritz-Carlton Hotel CEO and general-manager Andrew Torriani understated .
&amp;ldquo ; This is such a huge industry in this city and country , and the ( coronavirus ) is having such a devastating effect on it and everything else .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Torriani had a sense of what was to come when he heard that Nestl&amp;eacute ; , one of the world&amp;rsquo ; s largest companies , had banned travel for its employees .
And then events just mushroomed everywhere &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; There has been a precipitous drop in occupancy here , &amp;rdquo ; he said .
&amp;ldquo ; We could really start to feel it three weeks ago with things plummeting overall .
Then came entertainment , sports events and conventions being cancelled .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The Ritz is also a popular destination for visiting NHL clubs , not to mention visiting entertainers , actors and production personnel as well as business execs from around the globe .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Everyone I&amp;rsquo ; ve talked to in the business across the country has also been effected .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; He pointed out that the hotel had been taking an intensive pro-active safety approach for a while , with doorknobs to key-cards being constantly scrubbed and hand sanitizers being placed everywhere .
The hotel&amp;rsquo ; s acclaimed restaurant Maison Boulud has been shut down for cautionary reasons .
As a consequence , staffing levels are also down , with employees on temporary leave .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;img src= " https : **33;22284;TOOLONG .
title= " Shoppers and a renovation work crew are shown at Fairview shopping mall in Pointe-Claire at lunchtime on Monday , March 16 , 2020 .
" alt= " Shoppers and a renovation work crew are shown at Fairview shopping mall in Pointe-Claire at lunchtime on Monday , March 16 , 2020 .
" data-portal-copyright= " Peter McCabe " **28;22319;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1748349 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Unfortunately , we just don&amp;rsquo ; t have the volumes , but , hopefully , after this pause , we can get back to business as usual .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; With the Grand Prix and summer festival plans still in the works , this will be imperative for the survival for the tourism trade .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; I think Premier Legault has to be credited for taking tough measures now .
If we don&amp;rsquo ; t do this now , then we&amp;rsquo ; ll have another Italy , and that could be the end for so many and so much .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s a two-way street for tourism .
They&amp;rsquo ; re not coming here , and we&amp;rsquo ; re not going there .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Travel agent Genevi&amp;egrave ; ve Stachtchenko conceded she hasn&amp;rsquo ; t made &amp;ldquo ; a penny&amp;rdquo ; for a few weeks .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; No one is going anywhere these days , &amp;rdquo ; she said .
&amp;ldquo ; All I&amp;rsquo ; m doing now is cancelling tickets and reservations and trying to get refunds for customers .
Or else trying to get snowbird customers booked to come back later to come back now , but that&amp;rsquo ; s been so tough with many of those flights booked or being cut back .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; If I don&amp;rsquo ; t get some customers out from France within 48 hours , they could be facing many weeks of quarantine when they get back here .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Stachtchenko can&amp;rsquo ; t recall business ever being this abysmal .
Not even around 9/11 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; I was actually booking a lot of people then , but I can&amp;rsquo ; t see anyone booking for at least another month .
Still , I&amp;rsquo ; m sure I&amp;rsquo ; m far from the only one with zero income these days .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; No doubt .
There&amp;rsquo ; s an eerie emptiness at downtown shops .
So many businesses have curtailed operations for the time being , even though they aren&amp;rsquo ; t required to do so .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; There&amp;rsquo ; s no customers coming , so what&amp;rsquo ; s the point of staying open ? &amp;rdquo ; said one salesperson , whose shop was in the midst of closing .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Boutique Tozzi manager Ismael Oblitas acknowledged that business at his Crescent St .
shop had slowed down and he was anticipating more of a downturn in the next two weeks .
But he echoed the sentiments of other retailers offering a solution to those uneasy about showing up in person .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The best short-term solution would be to support businesses like ours and so many others through our online platforms , &amp;rdquo ; he said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The strategy appears to be working .
Canada Post mailman Tony Francescangeli has seen a huge upsurge of late in home deliveries of parcels from Amazon and other online operators : &amp;ldquo ; Neither snow nor rain , nor sleet nor heat , and , now , coronavirus can deter these packages from being delivered .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Lufa , the food delivery system with its urban rooftop vegetable farms , has , not surprisingly , also received a major sales boost .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Even though restaurants are permitted to stay open , albeit in diminished capacity , many are now shutting down entirely .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Time Out Market in the Eaton Centre announced that it will be closing down temporarily as of Tuesday .
Also starting Tuesday , Tim Hortons will close indoor seating at its outlets , offering only take-out , drive-thru and delivery .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Other restos , which have closed or planning to do , are also considering a similar tack , in providing take out service .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We&amp;rsquo ; re looking into it , &amp;rdquo ; said Stephen Leslie , whose two popular restaurants , Tavern on the Square and Monkland Tavern , are both closed .
&amp;ldquo ; But the situation is ever evolving , changing from hour to hour .
It&amp;rsquo ; s nuts .
I&amp;rsquo ; m now been hearing rumours about the SAQ closing .
If that happens , there will be tough days ahead for many .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Not everyone is bemoaning bad business .
With interest rates about as low as they&amp;rsquo ; ve been and with many wishing not to place their cash in the stock market , they are choosing brick and mortar investments instead .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; That happened during the financial crisis in 2008 , and I can see it happening now , &amp;rdquo ; noted Joseph Montanaro , among the city&amp;rsquo ; s premier real-estate agents .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; He reports having completed 10 offers for homes during spring break .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; I haven&amp;rsquo ; t been seeing panic in real estate .
In fact , I foresee an amazing season , especially if they slash the interest rates even further , which I think they will .
There are many taking advantage of the opportunities .
It&amp;rsquo ; s going to make a hot market even hotter .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; But nothing is gained anywhere if people keep freaking out .
We simply can&amp;rsquo ; t let things grind to a halt .

What 's open and closed in **29;22764;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Bill Brownstein , Montreal GazetteMon , 16 Mar 2020 22:26:17 **45;22795;TOOLONG .
BusinessLocal NewsNewsReal EstateRetailWorldDunlevy : It started as a cough , and led to a test for COVID-19http : **32;22842;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;22876;TOOLONG .
title= " Isolation cubicles at the COVID-19 testing centre in the former H ? tel-Dieu hospital .
" alt= " Isolation cubicles at the COVID-19 testing centre in the former H ? tel-Dieu hospital .
" data-portal-copyright= " Allen McInnis " **28;22911;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1744944 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;22941;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; It began with a cough .
A solitary cough , in the night .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; I was lying in bed at my friend Rupert&amp;rsquo ; s place in the south of England , on a stopover on my way back from covering the &lt;a href= " https : **33;22977;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Berlinale , a .
the Berlin International Film Festival .
&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It was Thur .
, Feb .
27 , a more innocent time , seemingly ages removed from the current COVID-19 world lockdown .
Rupert and I had spent the day hiking the hills , ocean-side cliffs and wetlands of the area .
Rupert had a cough , and apparently I had caught it .
Or had I ? Perhaps my throat was dry .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The next day , I was due to fly back .
After lunch with Rupert and his sister at a vegan restaurant , I stopped into the small-town pharmacy next door and purchased a surgical mask at the cost of four British pounds , or $7 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; I was not concerned about the cough which I may or may not have caught &amp;mdash ; and which I was certain was not COVID-19 &amp;mdash ; but about protecting myself from other travellers carrying the virus on the flight home .
My wife lives with an autoimmune disease , and I was determined to stay safe .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; I was one of just a few passengers on our British Airways flight to do so , much to the consternation of my seat-mate , who eyed me cautiously despite the empty seat between us and my unsuccessful attempt at small-talk .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; I landed in Montreal , ditched the mask , cleaned my hands with Purell , took a cab home from the airport , and kissed my wife .
Agreed , that last part probably wasn&amp;rsquo ; t the smartest thing to do .
But remember , we&amp;rsquo ; re talking almost three weeks ago .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Turns out I did have a cough , and it soon became nasty .
But I never had a fever , and the COVID-19-related information at the time said symptoms were cough plus fever plus trouble breathing , etc .
And my wife never caught it , so we weren&amp;rsquo ; t worried .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The cough stuck around , forcing me to take a couple of sick days and leaving me at half-capacity when I tried to stage a comeback , even while working from home .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Which brings us up to last week , &lt;a href= " https : **33;23012;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;when each day seemed to take the COVID-19 protocol into new&lt;/a&gt; , unknown territory .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Upping the ante , my wife&amp;rsquo ; s parents were driving in from Ottawa to see her final exhibition for her master&amp;rsquo ; s degree in visual arts .
And they were planning to stay with us .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Things were ramping up , both in Quebec and internationally .
There was a moment of truth , as we wondered whether to have her parents come &amp;mdash ; but I still had no fever , therefore no COVID-19 , and she hadn&amp;rsquo ; t caught my cough , so I surely wasn&amp;rsquo ; t contagious anymore ; we went ahead , albeit cautiously .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; I stifled my cough &amp;mdash ; coughing only once all evening , going into our bedroom to do so &amp;mdash ; and washed my hands repeatedly .
I avoided kisses , hugs and all bodily contact .
We chatted , ate dinner and retired for the evening .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Then , after hearing over the course of the day about the &lt;a href= " https : **33;23047;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;NBA season being postponed&lt;/a&gt; , &lt;a href= " https : **33;23082;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Sophie Gr ? goire Trudeau being in self-isolation&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href= " https : **33;23117;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Tom Hanks and his wife having COVID-19&lt;/a&gt; , we saw that Quebec had changed its guidelines for getting tested : from having cough and fever and trouble breathing , to cough OR fever OR trouble breathing .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " https : **33;23152;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;I called 811&lt;/a&gt; around 10:30 p .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; After 51 minutes on hold , a nurse answered .
She asked a bunch of questions , and informed me that since I had been out of the country and was experiencing symptoms , I should get tested .
She would call the COVID-19 testing clinic at the former &lt;a href= " https : **33;23187;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;H ? tel-Dieu hospital&lt;/a&gt; on Thursday morning and they would call me for an appointment .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; I messaged Rupert to see if he had got over his cough , and went to bed .
I woke up early Thursday and was relieved to read his reply .
Not only had he fully recovered , but no one around him had caught it &amp;mdash ; not even his parents , whose home he and his sister had slept at on the day he dropped me at the airport .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Still , feeling increasingly overwhelmed by world events and the outside chance that we may have just unknowingly infected my septuagenarian in-laws with COVID-19 , we suggested they head back to Ottawa that day , instead of Friday .
It didn&amp;rsquo ; t take much convincing .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Then we waited .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; By Thursday afternoon , wondering if I had been forgotten , I called 811 , only to hear a message saying the line was &amp;ldquo ; unavailable .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Same thing Friday , and no luck getting through to the alternate 877 number that had been set up .
And still no call .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; By Saturday , we had pretty much given up hope .
After 15 days since my return , I was almost over my cough and my wife still hadn&amp;rsquo ; t caught it , so the odds appeared to be on our side .
Still .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; And we were worried about her parents .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Finally , at 1:48 p .
, the call came .
I was told to go to the H&amp;ocirc ; tel-Dieu clinic on Sunday evening to be tested .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; I write these lines on Monday afternoon , in limbo while awaiting the results , which could take from 24 hours to a few days .
Stay tuned for a follow-up column detailing the testing process , and to find out , along with me , whether I merely had a close call or I have become Quebec&amp;rsquo ; s latest case of COVID-19 .

&lt;/p&gt; T'Cha Dunlevy , Montreal GazetteMon , 16 Mar 2020 22:25:05 **45;23800;TOOLONG .
NewsFitness : Do you have what it takes to be an ultra-marathoner ? http : //montrealgazette .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;23847;TOOLONG .
title= " " You have to want to keep going and continually find reasons to keep going , " says Cynthia Fish .
A veteran of 20 ultras , the 59-year-old Montrealer has tackled the 6633 Arctic Ultra -- billed as " the world 's most extreme ultra-marathon " -- twice .
" alt= " " You have to want to keep going and continually find reasons to keep going , " says Cynthia Fish .
A veteran of 20 ultras , the 59-year-old Montrealer has tackled the 6633 Arctic Ultra -- billed as " the world 's most extreme ultra-marathon " -- twice .
" data-portal-copyright= " 6633 Arctic Ultra " **28;23882;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1744932 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;23912;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span style= " font-family : -apple-system , BlinkMacSystemFont , ' Segoe UI ' , Roboto , Oxygen-Sans , Ubuntu , Cantarell , ' Helvetica Neue ' , sans-serif ; " &gt;Ever wonder what drives those crazy humans who compete in ultra-marathons , arguably the most gruelling physical undertaking that charges a registration fee ? Is their motivation based on a burning need to test themselves against the trifecta of challenges -- extreme distance , extreme temperature and extreme terrain ? Or is it an overgrown sense of adventure that takes them to the middle of the desert , the outer reaches of the Arctic , deep in the jungle or high in the mountains ? &lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; To find out more about what makes ultra-marathoners tick , &lt;a href= " https : **33;23948;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;a team of Scottish and American researchers gathered information&lt;/a&gt; on 12 competitors ( nine men and three women ) in the 6633 Arctic Ultra , a 120-mile , three-day race through the Yukon where participants pull their food , clothes , sleeping bag and other supplies on a sled as they cross the Arctic Circle in sub-zero temperatures with bone-chilling wind .
The researchers&amp;rsquo ; objective was to document the injuries , sleep habits and mood of ultra-marathoners , thereby determining the degree of mental and physical toughness needed to compete .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Exploring the physiological and psychological fortitude of ultra-marathoners is no small task , given the difficulty and expense of collecting data in real time .
Combine that with the small pool of those who register in each event and the high percentage of those who don&amp;rsquo ; t finish , and it&amp;rsquo ; s no wonder there&amp;rsquo ; s very little that&amp;rsquo ; s known about the psyche of athletes for whom no challenge is too great .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Cynthia Fish , a 59-year-old Montrealer , knows first-hand what it takes to conquer great distances in weather and terrain that would scare most of us silly .
A veteran of 20 ultras , she has tackled the 6633 Arctic Ultra &amp;mdash ; billed as &amp;ldquo ; the world&amp;rsquo ; s most extreme ultra-marathon&amp;rdquo ; &amp;mdash ; twice .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Any mistake you make can be really dangerous , so your mind is constantly busy , &amp;rdquo ; she said of the 193-kilometre trek .
&amp;ldquo ; You also spend a lot of time doing body checks : knees , feet , hips &amp;mdash ; there isn&amp;rsquo ; t a piece of your body that doesn&amp;rsquo ; t hurt .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Turns out her experience is typical for ultra-marathoners .
Ten of the 12 Arctic race participants monitored by the researchers were injured ; eight reported multiple injuries .
Hip , back , knee and shin pain , scrapes , diarrhea , vomiting , blisters and frostbite were typical , with almost half the racers reporting that their injuries lasted multiple days .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The pain moves around the body , &amp;rdquo ; said Fish .
&amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s when it stays there for a long time that it becomes a problem .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Racers averaged four hours of sleep during the three-day race .
Fish says the lack of sleep was the toughest part , noting she got about six hours of shut-eye between the start and finish lines .
Fish counts on sleep to help her recover physically and mentally , which is why she finds ultra-marathons that have a 24-hour running clock more challenging than ones that suspend the race overnight .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; As important as sleep is , mental toughness is the secret sauce of ultra-marathoners .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; While previous research has suggested that individual athletes should more adequately prepare sleep strategies in order to enhance their performance , &amp;rdquo ; the research team wrote , &amp;ldquo ; this study provides evidence that strategies improving mental toughness may be more pertinent , particularly as there are performance advantages with spending less time sleeping if it can be handled effectively .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Fish also suggests having confidence in your training is a huge advantage .
When the going gets tough , she knows her body is up to the challenge , which allows her to draw on her mental reserves to keep putting one foot in front of the other .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; If you second-guess your training and ability , you fail , &amp;rdquo ; she said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Also important is having the right gear for the right conditions , which in the case of the Arctic race means knowing how to dress for cold-weather exercise &amp;mdash ; something most Canadians have grown up learning .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; A lot of people show up ( to the race ) thinking that the cold is the problem , but it&amp;rsquo ; s the sweat that gets them in the end , &amp;rdquo ; Fish said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Clothes that are dampened by sweat during the day freeze when the sun goes down or the temperature drops .
The trick to staying dry is knowing which clothes to wear when , and changing on the fly .
Fish practised this repeatedly during winter training sessions .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; For those who are well prepared , well dressed and well trained , crossing the finish line &amp;ldquo ; is all mental , &amp;rdquo ; she said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; You have to want to keep going and continually find reasons to keep going , &amp;rdquo ; Fish said of the mentality of a successful ultra-marathoner .
&amp;ldquo ; No one is super-fast in these races , so it&amp;rsquo ; s not exhaustion that causes people to quit .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Fish relies on patience and determination to see the race through to the end .
She also finds a type of serenity during an ultra event , which helps her navigate the tough parts of the course .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s rare that you get that much quality time with absolutely no responsibilities , &amp;rdquo ; she said .
&amp;ldquo ; That&amp;rsquo ; s the pleasure for me .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Said like a born ultra-marathoner .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;23983;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;24025;TOOLONG .

Runners need to find an alternative route in case of **27;24123;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;24152;TOOLONG .
from Jill **27;24187;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Jill Barker , Special to Montreal GazetteSun , 15 Mar 2020 14:37:36 **45;24216;TOOLONG &amp;amp ; **25;24263;TOOLONG artists in limbo after coronavirus cancellationshttp : **27;24290;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;24319;TOOLONG .
title= " Montreal electronic duo Pelada : Chris Vargas ( left ) and Tobias Rochman .
" alt= " Montreal electronic duo Pelada : Chris Vargas ( left ) and Tobias Rochman .
" data-portal-copyright= " Rebecca Storm " **28;24354;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1746314 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;24384;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; This was supposed to be a breakthrough spring tour in Europe and North America for Montreal-based underground electronic music duo Pelada .
Instead , Tobias Rochman and Chris Vargas are stuck in a Brussels hotel , watching show after show get cancelled due to the COVID-19 outbreak .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Major music festivals such as Coachella in California and &lt;a href= " http : **34;24420;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;South by Southwest ( SXSW ) in Texas&lt;/a&gt; have been postponed or cancelled , depriving already financially precarious artists dependent on touring the ability to make ends meet .
On Thursday , Montreal &lt;a href= " https : **33;24456;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;promoter Evenko suspended all shows with 250 or more people&lt;/a&gt; for the next 30 days based on measures put in place by the provincial government .
The Orchestre symphonique de Montr&amp;eacute ; al ( OSM ) cancelled 11 concerts until April 5 , and their appearance with Kent Nagano at Carnegie Hall in New York March 24 will no longer happen .
Popular Montreal indie band Wolf Parade scrapped its upcoming European tour .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; While major concert promoters and venues are feeling the effects , for many smaller local artists the inability to tour can be career-threatening .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; After six years as a group , this would have been our first profitable tour , &amp;rdquo ; Rochman said Thursday via Skype from Brussels , where they had unexpectedly camped the last three days .
&amp;ldquo ; This was our first time working with a more professional agency out of the U .
We were looking forward to this tour as the first major one after being signed and putting out our record .
The shows we&amp;rsquo ; re playing are of a higher profile , with better pay .
We&amp;rsquo ; ve been planning for this tour for more than a year .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Pelada , who released the critically acclaimed Movimiento Para Cambio in October , were supposed to start the 15-date first leg of their European tour in Italy .
That show was cancelled , as was their weekend show in Russia , which required they pay for a work visa upfront .
They ended up in Brussels and were due to make their way Friday to Switzerland .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; With their shows not going as planned and those expected guarantees &amp;mdash ; normally paid out after the show &amp;mdash ; gone , even an extra $140 for a hotel stay in Belgium can be a financial strain .
Flights , trains and buses are other costs bands pay for in advance , and being able to exchange them for a later date isn&amp;rsquo ; t always a help .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Before we came , we applied for P-2 visa work permits for the United States because while we were gone , we needed it to process before our show April 17 at UCLA , &amp;rdquo ; said Vargas .
&amp;ldquo ; That was around $2,000 we needed to make sure that was processed while we were here .
And it&amp;rsquo ; s not even a guarantee we get the visa .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Added Rochman : &amp;ldquo ; We&amp;rsquo ; d be fine going home , but we don&amp;rsquo ; t even have the means to do that .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The band was set to play high-profile festivals like Primavera in Spain and Rewire in the Netherlands .
With a touring itinerary set to last through the summer , Rochman and Vargas left their day jobs to pursue music full-time .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; When you&amp;rsquo ; re living right on the threshold of profitability , it can be very dangerous , &amp;rdquo ; said Rochman .
&amp;ldquo ; We&amp;rsquo ; re in the gig economy , and the reality of seeing that bubble burst is devastating .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Micha&amp;euml ; l Bardier books and manages local and international artists with his Montreal company Heavy Trip .
He estimates he&amp;rsquo ; s lost $250,000 in guarantees for his acts so far , in addition to flights and other costs .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Honestly , the company has been in a good position lately .
We&amp;rsquo ; ve been booking bigger tours in the U .
and Europe , &amp;rdquo ; Bardier said .
&amp;ldquo ; We&amp;rsquo ; re not going to put the key in the door , but for sure , this is rough .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; An added problem for Bardier and many others is bands route their tours around major North American festivals in the spring such as SXSW , Big Ears in Nashville and Mission Creek Festival in Iowa .
All three have been cancelled .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Honestly , it&amp;rsquo ; s just really bad timing because last year around this time , I really determined March and April to be a really good period for international , experimental , world and jazz to tour in North America , so I really gave everything I had to route these tours , &amp;rdquo ; Bardier said .
Right now everyone is scrambling to move their dates to the fall , when things will presumably be better .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; One artist set to play SXSW was Montreal rapper Naya Ali .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s actually been a long time dream of mine to attend , let alone perform at SXSW .
It would have been a solid foot in door in the U .
market , &amp;rdquo ; Ali said .
&amp;ldquo ; However , I completely understand the seriousness of the situation and the measures that are being taken to protect all of our health .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;24491;TOOLONG .
