the latest in our coronavirus **29;24568;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Erik Leijon , Special to Montreal GazetteSat , 14 Mar 2020 10:00:19 **45;24599;TOOLONG .
ArtsLocal NewsMusicNewsQuebec shuts down as Premier Fran ? ois Legault declares an emergencyhttp : **31;24646;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;24679;TOOLONG .
title= " Quebec Premier Fran ? ois Legault has called on organizers of events that would attract more than 250 people to cancel them .
" alt= " Quebec Premier Fran ? ois Legault has called on organizers of events that would attract more than 250 people to cancel them .
" data-portal-copyright= " Dave Sidaway " **28;24714;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1742332 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; QUEBEC &amp;mdash ; Declaring Quebec in an emergency situation that requires decisive acts and sacrifices by all , the Legault government Thursday announced a series of tough , sweeping measures designed to curb the spread of the &lt;a href= " http : **34;24744;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;novel coronavirus&lt;/a&gt; before it gets out of hand .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; And the orders could get more draconian &amp;mdash ; from closing schools and shopping malls to a generalized quarantine of the island of Montreal , Quebec&amp;rsquo ; s most populated city .
The province has the power to do it all if necessary and rules nothing out as it tries to keep the number of cases down .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; &lt;a href= " http : **34;24780;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;I am asking a lot&lt;/a&gt; , &amp;rdquo ; Premier Fran&amp;ccedil ; ois Legault conceded at a news conference where the new measures were announced now that Quebec has 17 confirmed cases of the virus &amp;mdash ; thus far all travellers who came home with the virus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We have a major challenge and if we want to succeed I need the help of all Quebecers .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Today , Quebec must put itself on an emergency footing .
Our challenge in the coming weeks to contain the spread of the virus .
The coming weeks will be critical .
Our goal is slow the spread of the virus to the maximum .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Priority 1 is public health .
We have to protect ourselves and the best way to protect those we love is to protect ourselves .
I am calling on the solidarity of Quebecers , on the sense of responsibility of everyone .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Legault also warned Quebecers to brace for the long haul : months not weeks of disturbances in their lives .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The coming weeks will be critical in terms of the virus spreading .
But we have to be realistic .
We are facing a crisis that will last for months .
We must prepare .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Earlier , in the legislature , he said : &amp;ldquo ; The coming months are going to be very difficult , very difficult for our health network , very difficult for the Quebec economy .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The government plan &amp;mdash ; which was followed by a string of other cancellations and closings by cities and groups across Quebec &amp;mdash ; is stern stuff , but less harsh compared with acts taken by the rest of the planet .
Quebec , for example , has not closed public schools , while Ontario has &amp;mdash ; until April 5 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We are not asking that schools be closed at this time , &amp;rdquo ; Education Minister Jean-Fran&amp;ccedil ; ois Roberge told reporters .
&amp;ldquo ; As the premier said , nothing is excluded at this time .
We are assessing the situation .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; One reason the province is holding back is because there has not yet been a confirmed transmission on Quebec soil .
It will happen , warned Quebec&amp;rsquo ; s director of public health , Horacio Arruda , who sat at the premier&amp;rsquo ; s side .
It&amp;rsquo ; s just a matter of time .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Quebec estimates between 30 and 70 per cent of the population could be affected by the virus , which Arruda noted is tougher to fight than the regular flu because humans have no antibodies to resist it .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; He added the very nature of the virus means strong measures are required immediately , even though the chance of getting it remains slim .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Actually , for Quebecers , if they have not travelled outside , the risk is not zero but almost zero , &amp;rdquo ; Arruda said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We are not in a crisis because we have not lost control of the situation , &amp;rdquo ; Arruda said .
&amp;ldquo ; What we want to do is prevent a crisis .
That&amp;rsquo ; s why we went with strong ( measures ) early .
All these things will reduce the risk of having a high curve ( of patients ) .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; He warned public health laws also give him sweeping powers .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s clear we will be violating the rights of individuals , but it is for the collective good and the good of people , &amp;rdquo ; said Arruda .
&amp;ldquo ; Our system requires the solidarity of everyone .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; But for now , the measures announced are as follows : &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;mdash ; Legault is asking anyone who has returned to Quebec from any part of the world or who has flu symptoms to &lt;a href= " http : **34;24816;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;self-isolate for 14 days&lt;/a&gt; to slow the spread of the coronavirus .
The measure is applicable as of Thursday , not retroactively .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;mdash ; Health-care workers have no choice and are &lt;a href= " http : **34;24852;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;ordered to **25;24888;TOOLONG .
Public-sector workers who self-isolate will be paid , Legault said .
Quebec will announce a financial package for the private sector in the coming days , but workers who are able should try and work from home .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;mdash ; The government will announce measures to help businesses who are affected by solvency issues at a later date .
&amp;ldquo ; We won&amp;rsquo ; t leave anyone behind , &amp;rdquo ; Legault said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;mdash ; Organizers of indoor events that attract &lt;a href= " http : **34;24915;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;more than 250 people&lt;/a&gt; are ordered to cancel them for the next 30 days .
Any other events deemed not essential can also be cancelled .
Public schools will not be closed for the time being , but the government is ruling nothing out .
For now it is asking them to limit large group activities or eating together at the same time in the cafeteria .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;mdash ; Moments after the announcement , the &lt;a href= " http : **34;24951;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;National Hockey League&lt;/a&gt; joined the National Basketball Association in &amp;ldquo ; pausing&amp;rdquo ; the rest of the season .
Other groups seemed to take the cue , were adding their events to the list of cancelled or postponed , including both Montreal&amp;rsquo ; s and Quebec City&amp;rsquo ; s &lt;a href= " https : **33;24987;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;St .
Patrick 's parades&lt;/a&gt; .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;mdash ; Montreal Mayor &lt;a href= " https : **33;25022;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Val ? rie Plante&lt;/a&gt; announced the closing of the city&amp;rsquo ; s arenas , pools and libraries , botanical gardens and planetarium , but not the m&amp;eacute ; tro because it is too essential for workers to get around .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;mdash ; Quebec&amp;rsquo ; s Catholic bishops also announced all Saturday and Sunday masses were being cancelled and the National Assembly suspended all visits from the public , even though parliament itself is still operating .
Overnight , hand sanitizer dispensers were installed at strategic locations and media events staged with a distance between reporters and politicians .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;blockquote class= " twitter-tweet " data-width= " 550 " data-dnt= " true " &gt;&lt;p lang= " fr " dir= " ltr " &gt;DIRECTIVES DES ? V ? QUES CATHOLIQUES DU QU ? BEC POUR ENDIGUER LA PROPAGATION DU COVID-19&lt;a href= " https : //t .

&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;mdash ; Legault also said Quebecers should think twice before visiting seniors in residences .

We are here to support you .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Quebec announced eight new cases of COVID-19 on Thursday , bringing the total to 17 .

&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/div&gt; &lt;/div&gt; &lt;/div&gt; &lt;/div&gt; Philip Authier , Montreal GazetteFri , 13 Mar 2020 01:57:43 **45;25849;TOOLONG .
and A : What to do if you think you have COVID-19http : **32;25896;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;25930;TOOLONG .
title= " A sign at Montreal 's Jewish General Hospital outlines precautions to be taken by staff members who may have been exposed to the coronavirus .
" alt= " A sign at Montreal 's Jewish General Hospital outlines precautions to be taken by staff members who may have been exposed to the coronavirus .
" data-portal-copyright= " Allen McInnis " **28;25965;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1737834 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;25995;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; It all starts with the insidious symptoms , almost masking those of the seasonal flu .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; You develop a dry cough and might run a fever .
In more severe cases , you find yourself suddenly with a shortness of breath .
What do you do ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The following is a Q and A , based on information gleaned from the websites of the Public Health Agency of Canada and the Quebec Health Ministry , along with statements from officials about the novel coronavirus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s also based on the assumption that for now , at least , there is no local transmission of the SARS-CoV-2 coronavirus , which causes what the World Health Organization has declared a full-fledged pandemic .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;If you develop flu symptoms , what do you do ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Call the government phone line ( 1-877-644-4545 ) to seek testing for COVID-19 .
Call the 811 Info-Sant&amp;eacute ; hotline if you want a nurse to go over symptoms with you over the phone .
If you have questions about the coronavirus , you are asked not to call 811 , but to call the general information health line : 1-877-644-4545 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Have you recently travelled abroad ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; If you have , you will be advised to visit one of the &lt;a href= " https : **33;26031;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;three COVID-19 screening clinics&lt;/a&gt; .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;What if you have n't travelled abroad ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The 811 nurse will ask you whether you might have come into contact with someone who has travelled .
The nurse will also ask about whether you have any pre-existing medical conditions like heart disease , asthma , diabetes or cancer .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; For the moment , Dr .
Horacio Arruda , Quebec&amp;rsquo ; s chief public health officer , has reiterated that there is no local transmission of the coronavirus .
However , authorities suspect that SARS-CoV-2 is probably already circulating in the community .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Still , authorities have not reported widespread community transmission yet .
When that occurs , the protocols will probably change .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Should the Info-Sant ? nurse book an appointment for you at the screening clinic at the old H ? tel-Dieu hospital at Pine Ave .
and St-Urbain St .
, what is likely to happen ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; You will be assessed by a nurse and doctor .
A swab will be taken of your mouth and throat and sent for analysis by the &lt;span class= " st " &gt;Laboratoire de sant ? publique du Qu ? bec .
It should take less than 24 hours to get a result back .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; In the meantime , you will be presumed to have contracted COVID-19 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;What if my symptoms at the clinic are severe ? What if I say I have difficulty breathing ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; You will probably be transferred to the &lt;a href= " https : **33;26066;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Jewish General Hospital&lt;/a&gt; for treatment and isolation .
The Jewish General is one of four designated COVID-19 treatment centres in the province .
Ste-Justine Hospital has been designated for children and teens with COVID-19 .
The evidence to date suggests that the potentially lethal respiratory illness has mostly spared young people .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s also possible that if you have difficulty breathing when you first call 811 , you could be transported by ambulance to the Jewish General .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;If my symptoms are not severe at the screening clinic , what can I then expect ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; You will be advised to return home and to self-isolate pending the results of the COVID-19 test .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; At this time , there is no vaccine for COVID-19 or any natural health products that are authorized to treat or protect against COVID-19 , &amp;rdquo ; according to the &lt;a href= " https : **33;26101;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Public Health Agency of Canada&lt;/a&gt; .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Most people with mild coronavirus illness will recover on their own .
Your health care provider may recommend steps you can take to relieve symptoms .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The nurse at the screening clinic will hand you a kit with two pairs of gloves and two N-95 respirator masks , along with &lt;a href= " https : **33;26136;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;five pages of typed instructions&lt;/a&gt; to follow while at home .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;What do those instructions say ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Do not go to school or work .
Do not visit a children&amp;rsquo ; s daycare or a long-term care centre .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Do not use public transit .
Postpone any non-urgent medical appointments .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Do not invite people to your home .
Stay alone in your home in the same room as often as possible .
Do not change rooms .
If possible , use a bathroom not frequented by anyone else .
This last instruction arises from preliminary research showing that the coronavirus spreads easiest within families .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Wear a mask whenever anyone else in your home is in the same room as you .
Use a paper tissue to cough , throw away the tissue afterward into a garbage container and then wash your hands .
If a paper tissue is not around , cough or sneeze into your sleeve or elbow .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Wash your hands often with soap and water for at least 20 seconds .
Do not share plates , utensils , glasses and towels with any other family member .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;This is important : &lt;/strong&gt; Take your temperature at the same time every day and keep written track of the readings .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;iframe src= " **40;26171;TOOLONG .
&lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;What happens if your symptoms worsen while at home ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Contact the Info-Sant&amp;eacute ; 811 hotline if you have &lt;em&gt;any&lt;/em&gt; of the following symptoms : fever , cough , shortness of breath , difficulty breathing , chest pain , severe diarrhea , you have vomited or suffer from unusual , severe fatigue .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; And remember to tell the Info-Sant&amp;eacute ; nurse that you are under investigation for COVID-19 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Depending on your answers , the nurse could recommend that you go to a hospital on your own wearing a mask and using personal transport .
It&amp;rsquo ; s also possible that an ambulance might pick you up .
The hospital , in all probability the Jewish General , will be notified in advance of your arrival .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; At any time , if your symptoms worsen , and you feel like your life is in danger , the health ministry says call 911 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;What if my symptoms do not worsen ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Continue to stay at home until you recover .
To date , officials have advised people to self-isolate for 14 days .
It&amp;rsquo ; s possible you might have to stay at home longer .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;What if I get stressed , become anxious or develop obsessive ideas that seem to take over my mind ? &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Call Info-Sant&amp;eacute ; and a psychosocial health professional will provide you with support and counselling depending on your needs .

&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;26473;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;26515;TOOLONG .
coronavirus **29;26550;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;26581;TOOLONG .

Trudeau and wife Sophie in self-isolation as she 's tested for **29;26689;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;26720;TOOLONG .
in Saskatoon cancelled over coronavirus **29;26755;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Aaron Derfel , Montreal GazetteThu , 12 Mar 2020 21:58:48 **45;26786;TOOLONG .
NewsQuebecChristopher Labos : Lung cancer screening can save liveshttp : **35;26833;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;26870;TOOLONG .
title= " A physician works with a patient in a CT scanner .
" Simulation studies suggest that if everyone eligible for lung cancer screening got yearly CT scans , you prevent just over 12,000 lung cancer deaths every year , " Christopher Labos writes .
" alt= " A physician works with a patient in a CT scanner .
" Simulation studies suggest that if everyone eligible for lung cancer screening got yearly CT scans , you prevent just over 12,000 lung cancer deaths every year , " Christopher Labos writes .
" data-portal-copyright= " Jim Cole " **28;26905;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1741880 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; Lung cancer remains the No .
1 cancer killer in the country .
Every year , lung cancer kills &lt;a href= " https : **33;26935;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;far more&lt;/a&gt; women than breast cancer and far more men than prostate cancer .
Its five-year &lt;a href= " https : **33;26970;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;survival rate&lt;/a&gt; is a depressingly low 19 per cent , compared to breast cancer ( 88 per cent ) or prostate cancer ( 93 per cent ) .
There is , however , something we can do to improve lung cancer outcomes .
The problem is we just don&amp;rsquo ; t do it .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The key to reducing cancer deaths is effective screening .
Screening for cervical cancer ( with Pap tests ) and colorectal cancer ( with colonoscopies and now with FIT testing ) has led to dramatic reductions in both of these cancers .
The point is to catch a pre-cancerous lesion and remove it before it can transform into a more aggressive cancer and metastasize through the body .
Unfortunately , not all cancers are amenable to screening .
For example , screening for prostate cancer with &lt;a href= " https : **33;27005;TOOLONG .
is more complicated than it might seem .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Likewise , screening for lung cancer is not very easy .
Intuitively , you would think that X-rays should catch lung tumours early , when they are still small and easily removable .
But data from studies like the &lt;a href= " https : **33;27040;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;PLCO&lt;/a&gt; trial have shown that regular chest X-rays do not reduce lung cancer mortality .
In fact , most &lt;a href= " https : **33;27075;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;guidelines&lt;/a&gt; recommend against using chest X-rays to screen for lung cancer because , apart from being largely ineffective , there are also significant downsides .
Cost and repeated radiation exposure are obvious negatives .
But the real danger associated with X-rays is that of over-diagnosis .
What can seem like a mass on an X-ray can turn out to be nothing after more scans and biopsies .
The rate of these false positives can be quite high .
In the &lt;a href= " https : **33;27110;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;National Lung Screening Trial , &lt;/a&gt; the false positive rate with annual X-rays was nearly 95 per cent .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The past few years have shown that CT scans may be a better option .
The National Lung Screening Trial compared low dose CT scans to standard X-rays and found that CT scans picked up more cancers and reduced lung cancer deaths from 309 to 247 deaths per 100,000 person-years .
While the rate of false positives was still high ( over 96 per cent ) , the mortality reduction convinced many people that screening with yearly CT scans was worth the effort .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Critics have pointed out that the reduction in mortality is relatively small , that the false-positive rate with CT scanning is still very high and that CT scans deliver even more radiation than X-rays .
But even if you account for the radiation delivered by CTs , you would still pick up &lt;a href= " https : **33;27145;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;108 lung cancers for every one cancer&lt;/a&gt; caused by the radiation .
In fact , simulation studies suggest that if everyone eligible for lung cancer screening got yearly CT scans , you prevent just over &lt;a href= " https : **33;27180;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;12,000 lung cancer deaths&lt;/a&gt; every year .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " https : **33;27215;TOOLONG .
class= " s1 " &gt;Guidelines &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class= " s1 " **36;27250;TOOLONG .
annual screening for three consecutive years with low-dose CT scans &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;for adults ages 55 to 74 ( U .
guidelines say 80 ) who have a history of heavy smoking and currently smoke , or quit less than 15 years ago .
Heavy smoking is usually defined as a smoking history of 30 pack-years ( one pack a day for 30 years , two packs a day for 15 years or three packs a day for 10 years ) .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Unfortunately , a U .
study found that &lt;a href= " https : **25;27288;TOOLONG : //www .
class= " s3 " &gt;seven out of eight **29;27315;TOOLONG who would qualify for lung cancer screening do not get it .
People have suggested that there is a bias against smokers , but I suspect most people are simply not aware of the guidelines .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Given how much attention we pay to breast cancer and prostate cancer screening , it is sometimes surprising we do not talk about lung cancer screening more , since lung cancer is actually more lethal .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;It would be good if people were aware of the guidelines and got screened if they meet the criteria .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class= " s2 " &gt;But&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt; it would be even better if they stopped smoking .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;em&gt;Christopher Labos&lt;/em&gt; &lt;em&gt; is a Montreal doctor and an associate with the McGill Office for Science and Society .
He also co-hosts a podcast called The Body of Evidence .
&lt;/em&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;27346;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;27388;TOOLONG .
columns by Christopher **26;27423;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Christopher Labos , Special to Montreal GazetteTue , 10 Mar 2020 15:56:52 **45;27451;TOOLONG .
It 's never too soon to embrace positive aginghttp : **35;27498;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;27535;TOOLONG .
title= " Students walk by McGill University 's library in 2015 .
Studies have shown that individuals with a university education have a greater life expectancy than those without .
" alt= " Students walk by McGill University 's library in 2015 .
Studies have shown that individuals with a university education have a greater life expectancy than those without .
" data-portal-copyright= " Marie-France Coallier " **28;27570;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1737149 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;27600;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; As an increasing number of Canadians enter their middle and golden years , there&amp;rsquo ; s less talk of finding the fountain of youth and more discussion around &lt;a href= " https : **33;27636;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;positive aging&lt;/a&gt; .
This shift in thinking is a welcome change from trying to turn back the clock , moving toward the more attainable goal of maintaining a high quality of life into retirement .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s not just boomers and Gen Xers who are hoping to redefine what it means to age .
Governments and municipalities understand that a healthy community of older adults puts less strain on public resources , which means they have a vested interest in keeping their aging citizens active and healthy .
And given that First World millennials and the generations that follow are expected to live to 100 , it&amp;rsquo ; s more important than ever to pursue a lifestyle devoted to healthy aging .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Philip Pizzo from the departments of pediatrics and microbiology/immunology at Stanford University penned &lt;a href= " https : **33;27671;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;an editorial in the Journal of the American Medical Association&lt;/a&gt; titled A Prescription for Longevity in the 21st Century .
His goal isn&amp;rsquo ; t just to add years to one&amp;rsquo ; s life , but to make the later decades of life &amp;ldquo ; more meaningful and functional and less attenuated to the morbidities that lead to medical , social and financial dependency .
&amp;rdquo ; In other words , he&amp;rsquo ; s touting the benefits of maintaining a healthy body , social life and bank account as the decades add up .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It seems obvious that Pizzo&amp;rsquo ; s prescription for longevity is directed at those in their middle years and beyond , but investing in longevity early will increase the odds of reaping the rewards from living a vibrant and purposeful life .
So don&amp;rsquo ; t wait until retirement looms to pursue the following life goals &amp;mdash ; it&amp;rsquo ; s never too early to embrace positive aging .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;Keep learning&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; Individuals with a university education have a greater life expectancy than those without .
Low levels of education often result in lower income ; according to American data , this results in a greater tendency toward declining physical and mental health , as well as an increase in unemployment .
Statistics suggest a 15-year difference in life expectancy between the richest and poorest Americans .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Urging the youngest generations to stay in school has been a common refrain , but catching up on missed education and the opportunities it offers never gets old .
Lifelong learning isn&amp;rsquo ; t just a stepping stone to good fiscal health &amp;mdash ; it&amp;rsquo ; s an important investment in living longer .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;Live life with purpose&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; Having a purpose beyond oneself &amp;mdash ; like caring for others , improving the world around you , sharing your expertise , getting involved in community groups and following a spiritual path &amp;mdash ; translates into a longer life , according to studies of the young and old .
Starting each day with a sense of purpose and a commitment to contributing to society is like a daily dose of medicine .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; With age comes more time to give of yourself , so the idea of creating opportunities for senior members of the community to share their experience and knowledge benefits society as a whole .
While retirement is often viewed as the end of your value , it&amp;rsquo ; s actually an opportunity to give more to society than you get back .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;Keep your friends close&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; Social connection is associated with a 50 per cent boost in survival .
Loneliness , on the other hand , can lead to increased risk of cardiovascular disease and stroke .
To put it more simply , &lt;a href= " https : **33;27706;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;having friends is good for your health&lt;/a&gt; .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Prioritizing relationships and staying engaged with family , friends , neighbours and co-workers is key to maintaining a high level of connectedness .
Yet there are plenty of times when isolation is common , including changing schools , jobs or cities ; separation from a spouse , partner or other family members ; and retirement .
Maintaining varied social networks allows for support during periods of change and reduces the risk of isolation .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;Adopt a healthy lifestyle&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s well known that exercising regularly , getting enough sleep and eating nutritious food improves health , well-being and longevity .
What&amp;rsquo ; s less understood is that adopting a healthy lifestyle is one of the only proven ways to reduce genetic risk factors like heart disease , obesity and mental illness .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Building healthy habits early also means enjoying the resulting energy , strength and positive mood on either side of middle age .
But the real payback comes during those years when age begins to whittle away at the physical and mental competencies we take for granted in youth .
Putting a priority on exercising , eating well and getting enough sleep slows down the physical decline , and is good for both mind and body .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;27741;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;27783;TOOLONG .

Runners need to find an alternative route in case of **27;27884;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;27913;TOOLONG .
from Jill **27;27948;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;27977;TOOLONG .
age in the eye : Daniel J .
Levitin on how to live well , not just **27;28012;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Jill Barker , Special to Montreal GazetteSun , 08 Mar 2020 11:36:40 **45;28041;TOOLONG &amp;amp ; **27;28088;TOOLONG : Is it the end of touchy-feely Montreal as we know it ? http : **37;28117;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;28156;TOOLONG .
title= " The good old days : Former Montreal boxing great Otis Grant plants a kiss on the cheek of former UFC champion Georges St-Pierre at the 15th Annual Sports Celebrity Breakfast Montreal Sunday , April 7 , 2019 at the Cummings Jewish Centre .
" alt= " The good old days : Former Montreal boxing great Otis Grant plants a kiss on the cheek of former UFC champion Georges St-Pierre at the 15th Annual Sports Celebrity Breakfast Montreal Sunday , April 7 , 2019 at the Cummings Jewish Centre .
" data-portal-copyright= " John Kenney " **28;28191;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1738767 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; At first glance , it looked like the two women were performing an elaborate Irish dance ritual at the downtown bar , perhaps in anticipation of their Riverdance moment .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It was quite fetching .
They approached one another almost ballet-like , bodies upright before bending down in perfect unison .
Then they stood up erect again .
Their arms bent and firmly tucked into their sides , each next slowly lifted a foot and , ever so gently , did a quick boot tap together .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Quite the performance , and so exquisitely choreographed as well .
A few observers felt inclined to applaud .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Curious , I asked about the nature of this impromptu recital .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; No recital , &amp;rdquo ; said one .
&amp;ldquo ; A salutation , &amp;rdquo ; said the other .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Whaat ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Say bye-bye to the two-cheek kiss and the fist bump .
And forget about the handshake &amp;mdash ; that&amp;rsquo ; s ancient history these days .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Say hey to the foot pump now .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; And say hey to the new reality in our present fearful times .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; I have since seen foot-pump &amp;mdash ; shoe-tap , for the more genteel among us &amp;mdash ; exchanges elsewhere in town .
It is , in fact , a trend that has been sweeping other parts of the planet of late .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Certainly , life is changing fast in Montreal , in what was once among the most touchy-feely spots on the continent .
Credit coronavirus angst for this extreme penchant for personal cleanliness .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Naively , I asked one of the women why they couldn&amp;rsquo ; t exchange elbow pumps .
I should have guessed what kind of response I would get .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Because we sneeze into our elbows , silly , &amp;rdquo ; one explained .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Of course .
My bad .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; As someone who spends considerable time pounding hardly antiseptic city pavement , I didn&amp;rsquo ; t have the heart to tell the women they had best wipe down their boots &amp;mdash ; and their hands &amp;mdash ; with disinfectant following a day of foot pumps .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It had to be a first this week when Quebec Health Minister Danielle McCann declared that citizens should back off two-cheek kisses , especially to the elderly and those prone to picking up viruses .
For the time being , anyway .
In lieu of handshakes and elbow , fist or foot pumps , McCann suggested simply blowing kisses to people .
Sensible advice &amp;mdash ; as long as one doesn&amp;rsquo ; t blow too hard and inadvertently transmit nasty stuff in one&amp;rsquo ; s breath to others .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Not to detract from the importance of personal hygiene these days , but where does it all end ? HAZMAT suits for all ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Some of us can recall our parents telling us to play outside in the dirt in order for us to build up our immune systems .
Were they trying to kill us ? OK , maybe in my case , because , in fairness , I was trouble as a tyke .
But not the rest of you .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s scary now .
Particularly because so many people are so freaked out .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The upshot is that manufacturers of hand sanitizers and face masks are among the few that are profiting these days .
Supermarket shelves are quickly emptying as panicked consumers hoard supplies .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Schools are being closed in parts of the world .
Vacations are being cancelled .
Cruise lines are singing the blues .
Baseball , basketball , soccer and sumo events abroad are being played out in arenas and stadiums that have been closed to the cheering hordes .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; How much longer will it be until sporting events on this continent follow suit ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; They&amp;rsquo ; ve even postponed the premi&amp;egrave ; re of the latest James Bond flick , No Time to Die , from April to November because of a presumed worldwide fear of assembling in multiplexes .
Hell , James Bond is supposed to save us all from nefarious germs , humanoids or otherwise ! What kind of message is this sending when we put our superheroes on hold ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Environmentally aware java lovers are understandably miffed with a new edict that has come down from Starbucks command-central .
The coffee chain has announced that customers are being temporarily barred from bringing their own personal mugs to its North American stores &amp;ldquo ; to help prevent the spread of coronavirus .
&amp;rdquo ; Instead , patrons will have to make do with paper cups for a spell .
However , the company will offer its 10-cent discount to customers who come in with their own mugs &amp;mdash ; even though they won&amp;rsquo ; t be able to use them .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Even the politically incorrect are holding back .
Weird Al Yankovic now refuses to perform My Corona , despite the fact his parody of The Knack hit My Sharona would really go viral .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; But no worries about one of my fave concert venues , the Corona Theatre .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s just a name , &amp;rdquo ; Evenko&amp;rsquo ; s Philip Vanden Brande says .
&amp;ldquo ; The theatre has been around a lot longer than the virus .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Vanden Brande notes that Evenko is monitoring the coronavirus situation closely , as it affects its venues like the Bell Centre and Corona , among others .
Should the situation evolve , Evenko will follow the advice of the minister of health and social services .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The health and safety of our fans are our highest priorities and we will implement all necessary safety measures as required , &amp;rdquo ; Vanden Brande says .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; In the interim , perhaps many would do well to chill a little and kick back with a Corona brew .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; And pay no heed to a recent , misleading PR poll of 737 American beer drinkers that reported that 38 per cent wouldn&amp;rsquo ; t purchase the Mexican suds .
It wasn&amp;rsquo ; t the coronavirus dictating their decision , but merely the fact they preferred other beers .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Actually , only four per cent of the deep thinkers polled equated Corona with coronavirus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Phew .
There may be some hope for humanity after all .

&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; Your favourite travel mug may be the latest casualty of the coronavirus outbreak .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; To combat the spread of the novel coronavirus , the coffee chain is not accepting reusable cups .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s a coronavirus thing , &amp;rdquo ; a barista at a Little Burgundy outlet told a customer on Thursday morning .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; In an &lt;a href= " https : **33;28620;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;open letter&lt;/a&gt; published Wednesday , executive vice-president Rossann Williams said the company is &amp;ldquo ; pausing the use of personal cups and &amp;lsquo ; for here&amp;rsquo ; ware&amp;rdquo ; as part of its response to the spread of coronavirus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The coffee chain is also ramping up regular cleaning practices across all stores , modifying or postponing large meetings and providing info to employees on how to respond to suspected cases of the virus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Starbucks has long offered a 10-cent discount to customers who bring their own reusable mugs or ask to use an in-store mug as part of a sustainability initiative .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The company says it will still offer the discount to customers who ask to use their reusable cup , or to use an in-store mug .

&amp;nbsp ; A second probable case was &lt;a href= " https : **33;28690;TOOLONG .

team tracking the coronavirushttp : **29;29151;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;29182;TOOLONG .
title= " " I would n't call this a pandemic just yet .
We would still have to wait a few months to make that kind of determination , " says epidemiologist John Brownstein .
" alt= " " I would n't call this a pandemic just yet .
We would still have to wait a few months to make that kind of determination , " says epidemiologist John Brownstein .
" data-portal-copyright= " Courtesy of Boston Children 's Hospital " **28;29217;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1737862 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;29247;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; An epidemiologist from Montreal has been at the forefront of tracking down the &lt;a href= " https : **33;29283;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **25;29318;TOOLONG spread .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; John Brownstein , the chief innovation officer at Boston Children&amp;rsquo ; s Hospital and a Harvard professor , is a founder , creator and head of the hospital&amp;rsquo ; s &lt;a href= " https : //healthmap .
" target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;HealthMap&lt;/a&gt; AI team , which was the first to alert the public , outside China , about some then-unidentified pneumonia-like cases in Wuhan on Dec .
The team then alerted the World Health Organization ( WHO ) to the situation , and now the whole world is abundantly aware .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; ( Full disclosure : John Brownstein is my way , way smarter yet most affable and unassuming nephew , who has been a guest on myriad U .
TV talk shows and interviewed in newspapers across the continent .
) &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Nor does the coronavirus mark the first time Brownstein&amp;rsquo ; s HealthMap team has delved into deadly viruses .
Since its creation in 2006 , it has dealt with everything from the avian and swine flu to MERS and Ebola .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 640 " height= " 360 " src= " https : **34;29345;TOOLONG .
frameborder= " 0 " allow= " accelerometer ; autoplay ; encrypted-media ; gyroscope ; picture-in-picture " **34;29381;TOOLONG &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Certainly , the coronavirus doesn&amp;rsquo ; t appear to be as deadly as Ebola , &amp;rdquo ; he says .
&amp;ldquo ; But it&amp;rsquo ; s the impact of the coronavirus on the elderly and those who are medically compromised that is of great concern .
All the same , I wouldn&amp;rsquo ; t call this a pandemic just yet .
We would still have to wait a few months to make that kind of determination .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Though some in the field have upped the mortality rate to three per cent of those with the virus , he cautions not to jump to conclusions .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We really have to be careful about the numbers we&amp;rsquo ; re putting out now .
The situation is incredibly fluid at the moment .
It depends on the underlying context , the capacity of the health system and the ability to differentiate between harsher and milder cases .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; What makes the coronavirus so complex to comprehend is that so much remains unknown about it .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We&amp;rsquo ; re still trying to understand the very features of the virus , how it is transmitted and spread , and whether or not it is symptomatic , &amp;rdquo ; he says .
&amp;ldquo ; The challenge is the transmission is very hard to control .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; He predicts a vaccine will become available , but , unfortunately , not soon enough to stop the spread .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Unlike most other major viral outbreaks , the coronavirus has created panic and paranoia in some parts of North America , largely because it&amp;rsquo ; s in the news 24/7 .
Many are scooping up &lt;a href= " https : //wp .
" target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;face masks ( which are n't deemed to be very helpful ) &lt;/a&gt; and hand sanitizers , emptying store shelves and hoarding food supplies , and avoiding crowds and restaurants &amp;mdash ; &lt;a href= " https : **33;29417;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;specifically Chinese eateries&lt;/a&gt; .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The resultant hysteria has been linked to disinformation coming from uninformed sources on the internet .
The HealthMap automated system is based on credible online news and social media reports as well as first-hand information from the field .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; There is just so much content and confusion out there .
We take all the credible data we have in our computer system in order to make a more accurate analysis of the situation .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Curiously , while his base of operations is Boston Children&amp;rsquo ; s Hospital , the coronavirus has had the least impact on kids , whose immune systems are often more ready for combat .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Our scope is essentially all ages .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Unlike some who have speculated that the coronavirus will disappear with the advent of warmer weather , he is not so optimistic , suggesting that , on some levels , it&amp;rsquo ; s not unlike a flu or cold that can strike any time .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; That&amp;rsquo ; s not really a hypothesis we can support right now .
It&amp;rsquo ; s really about exercising caution .
Certainly , it&amp;rsquo ; s always helpful to have supplies at home , and it can&amp;rsquo ; t be stated enough the importance of washing our hands .
But , honestly , I really believe we will get through this .
We&amp;rsquo ; ve seen worse .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;29452;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;29494;TOOLONG .

General Hospital ramps up preparations for a COVID-19 **29;29632;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;p&gt; After graduating from high school in Montreal , Brownstein earned a full scholarship to Yale University .
Following teaching and research assignments at Yale , he was hired at Harvard , where he became a full professor six years ago at the age of 36 .
He has been the chief innovation officer at Boston Children&amp;rsquo ; s Hospital for 15 years .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; AI has been such a boon to science and medicine , &amp;rdquo ; says Brownstein , who lives with his wife , Catherine , a geneticist and also a Harvard prof , and their two children , Jackson and Caroline .
&amp;ldquo ; I had always been fascinated by computer science growing up and how it could benefit our health system .
But I could never have anticipated the leaps AI has taken over the years and will continue to do so .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; All the same , he will never forsake his hometown .
He visits here several times a year to touch base with family , friends and the ever-burgeoning restaurant scene .
His biggest flaw probably is being an unabashed follower of the cursed New England Patriots .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; But given his contributions in helping stave off epidemics , he can be forgiven this trespass .

&lt;/p&gt; Bill Brownstein , Montreal GazetteThu , 05 Mar 2020 14:11:56 **45;29800;TOOLONG .
NewsTechnologyQuebec announces new Dorval residence for adults with special needshttp : **35;29847;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;29884;TOOLONG .
title= " Quebec Minister responsible for the Montr ? al region Chantal Rouleau was at the Lakeshore General Hospital in Pointe-Claire , March 3 , to announce the construction of a new type of housing for aging adults with special needs .
" alt= " Quebec Minister responsible for the Montr ? al region Chantal Rouleau was at the Lakeshore General Hospital in Pointe-Claire , March 3 , to announce the construction of a new type of housing for aging adults with special needs .
" data-portal-copyright= " " **28;29919;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1737173 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; A new type of residence will be built in the West Island to serve the aging adult population with special needs .
The idea is to create both a more humane living environment for this vulnerable group and a convivial working space for the staff who offers care and services .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Quebec Minister responsible for the Montr&amp;eacute ; al region Chantal Rouleau made the announcement on behalf of Quebec Minister responsible for Seniors and Informal Caregivers Marguerite Blais at the Lakeshore General Hospital in Pointe-Claire , Tuesday .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The need is immense for this kind of care , &amp;rdquo ; Rouleau said .
&amp;ldquo ; We are responding with concrete measures .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Described as &amp;ldquo ; alternative housing&amp;rdquo ; , the six-unit construction will house 72 aging adults with special needs .
The project will be built at 825 Dawson Ave .
, on land adjacent to the Batshaw Youth and Family Centre campus in Dorval .
The bilingual facility will have a staff of around 100 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Rouleau said the idea is to offer a more sensitive approach to long-term care , to create a facility that feels like a home .
Each resident will have a room with a private bathroom and there will be an emphasis on keeping the population active , both&amp;nbsp ; indoors and outdoors .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; I&amp;rsquo ; m happy that a facility is being built that respects the dignity of the aging population , &amp;rdquo ; said Liberal MNA for Marquette Enrico Ciccone .
Ciccone is the official opposition critic for sports , recreation and healthy living .
&amp;ldquo ; But with the shortage of manpower , especially in health care , my focus won&amp;rsquo ; t be on the brick and mortar .
It will be on the services being offered .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span style= " font-family : -apple-system , BlinkMacSystemFont , ' Segoe UI ' , Roboto , Oxygen-Sans , Ubuntu , Cantarell , ' Helvetica Neue ' , sans-serif ; " &gt;The project is part of the CAQ government 's commitment to invest $2 .
billion in the expansion of long-term care services in the province .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span style= " font-family : -apple-system , BlinkMacSystemFont , ' Segoe UI ' , Roboto , Oxygen-Sans , Ubuntu , Cantarell , ' Helvetica Neue ' , sans-serif ; " &gt;Rouleau said the government wants to build alternative housing and seniors facilities to house 2,600 more people , by 2022 .
And upgrades will be done to existing long-term facilities to accommodate an additional 2,500 patients .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; CIUSSS de l&amp;rsquo ; Ouest-de-l&amp;rsquo ; &amp;Icirc ; l .
general director Lynne McVey said the project was great news for the West Island health authority , which serves a population of around 500,000 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; There are 834 adults with special needs in our region and 144 of those adults are on a waiting list for special-needs housing , &amp;rdquo ; McVey said .
&amp;ldquo ; To be able to create a residence with a home-like environment for this vulnerable population is a wonderful gift from the government .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; McVey said the West Island CIUSSS had also received funding to subsidize families who want to offer foster care to adults with special needs .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The combination of the two ( initiatives ) works , &amp;rdquo ; McVey said .
&amp;ldquo ; Not all of the special-needs population has lost autonomy .
So they can be cared for in foster homes .
But when they begin to age , they need more help .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The budget for the Dorval project has yet to be determined , but will run somewhere between $35 and $50 million .
Rouleau said the goal is to have the facility up and running by 2022 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " **31;29949;TOOLONG " **38;29982;TOOLONG &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;30022;TOOLONG .

NewsSeniorsWest Island GazetteOpinion : Obesity should be viewed as a diseasehttp : **33;30313;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;30348;TOOLONG .
title= " " Many people think that those with obesity simply need to lose weight to be ' cured .
' Is it really that simple ? With obesity , there are a number of changes that occur in our bodies that make it difficult to lose weight , " Sylvia Santosa and David Secko write .
" alt= " " Many people think that those with obesity simply need to lose weight to be ' cured .
' Is it really that simple ? With obesity , there are a number of changes that occur in our bodies that make it difficult to lose weight , " Sylvia Santosa and David Secko write .
" data-portal-copyright= " Justin Sullivan " **28;30383;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1736779 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; On World Obesity Day , March 4 , organizers hope people will reflect on how obesity and being overweight affects more than 1 .
billion adults and 380 million children .
According to the World Health Organization , deaths worldwide from obesity and being overweight are more common than deaths from being underweight .
Though there are still many questions to be answered about obesity and obesity treatment , one thing seems clear : obesity is a disease that parallels aging .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Children with obesity can develop hypertension , high cholesterol and Type 2 diabetes .
These are conditions usually only seen in adults .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; People with obesity , on average , die about seven years earlier than those of normal weight .
We also know having obesity puts you at risk for many conditions and diseases , including Type 2 diabetes , impaired mobility , hypertension , sarcopenia , cardiovascular disease , cancer and Alzheimer&amp;rsquo ; s disease , all of which are also linked to aging .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Hit the molecular level and the linkage looks even more intimate .
In both aging and obesity , there is greater free radical formation , energy-producing mitochondria in our muscles start to fail and inflammation becomes chronic .
The immune cells in our body that fight infections also weaken with both obesity and aging .
Even our DNA is affected with obesity .
The telomeres that protect our DNA have been found to be shorter with obesity to a degree that aging is accelerated by eight years .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; But obesity is not just a condition that accelerates aging : obesity should be viewed as a disease that accelerates aging .
Obesity clearly changes the function of body systems resulting in adverse health outcomes , but there still is a debate over whether obesity is , in fact , a disease .
If you look at the definition of a disease , part of the controversy may surround the term &amp;ldquo ; normal functioning .
&amp;rdquo ; What is normal ? One could argue that weight gain and the eventual classification of obesity is a normal adaptation to energy surplus .
Here , some view obesity as arising from an unhealthy lifestyle , one that is fraught with too much food and too little exercise .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;30413;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;30455;TOOLONG .
is neglecting children suffering from obesity : **27;30490;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;30519;TOOLONG .
health professionals discriminate against obese people : **27;30554;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;30583;TOOLONG .
problem grows larger , costs Quebec $3B **29;30618;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;30649;TOOLONG .
Yes , you can be fat and fit , but that 's not the whole **26;30684;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;p&gt; Yet , there is no question as to whether other diseases associated with lifestyle are in fact diseases .
There is no debate over whether cardiovascular disease , cancer or Type 2 diabetes are diseases , even though they have significant lifestyle components .
One might respond that these diseases do not only result from lifestyle choices , but our genes as well .
But genes have also been linked with the development of obesity .
After all , don&amp;rsquo ; t we all have that friend that can eat twice the amount of food than we do and stay thin as a toothpick ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Many people think that those with obesity simply need to lose weight to be &amp;ldquo ; cured .
&amp;rdquo ; Is it really that simple ? With obesity , there are a number of changes that occur in our bodies that make it difficult to lose weight .
It is estimated that weight-loss treatment of obesity through lifestyle is successful in only 20 per cent of people .
Most who have kept off the weight will tell you that it is a lifelong struggle .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; We would argue that aging and obesity are actually two sides of the same coin .
The fact that so many people are affected means we need to act faster to address obesity .
Understanding obesity as a disease of premature aging might be the spark we need , for example , by applying abundant research in aging to obesity in order to generate new solutions .
Accepting obesity as a disease that accelerates aging will allow us to shift our approach to understanding obesity and its treatment .
And that new framing might bring a new awareness of the urgency to act on such a serious health threat .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;em&gt;Sylvia Santosa is an associate professor in the Department of Health , Kinesiology and Applied Physiology at Concordia University and a Canada Research Chair in Clinical Nutrition .
David Secko is a professor in , and chair of , Concordia 's Department of Journalism .

The passenger flew from Charles de Gaulle airport in Paris to Montreal&amp;rsquo ; s Trudeau airport on Feb .
25 before taking a connecting flight to Toronto&amp;rsquo ; s Pearson International , Lemay said in the memo , which was obtained by the Montreal Gazette and confirmed by Air Transat&amp;rsquo ; s parent company .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Following the announcement , Air Transat asked the flight attendants who worked the two&amp;nbsp ; flights in question to remain quarantined at home for 14 days .
It also informed pilots and mechanics who worked on the jets &amp;ldquo ; and recommended that they pay careful attention to their health for the appearance of any symptoms , &amp;rdquo ; according to the memo .

&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Air Transat informed airports and subcontractors of the situation .
The company &amp;ldquo ; completely disinfected&amp;rdquo ; the two aircraft concerned , according to the memo .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Be assured that the health of our employees and customers is always our greatest priority , &amp;rdquo ; Lemay said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Air Transat is monitoring the situation daily via its crisis cell and is applying recommendations from the Public Health Agency of Canada , he said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; New measures to better protect employees and passengers include creating safety reserves of masks , gloves and hand sanitizer ; sterilization kits in the event of a contagious passenger ; and a change in the procedure to replace air filters .
The company has also adjusted its protocol for suspected contagious illness aboard an aircraft .

BusinessLocal NewsJoe Schwarcz : Does drinking milk increase breast cancer risk ? http : **35;31384;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;31421;TOOLONG .
title= " Researchers from Loma Linda University concluded that even small amounts of milk , as little as one-third of a cup a day , can significantly raise the risk of breast cancer .
" alt= " Researchers from Loma Linda University concluded that even small amounts of milk , as little as one-third of a cup a day , can significantly raise the risk of breast cancer .
" data-portal-copyright= " Rob Carr " **28;31456;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1736088 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Is milk protective against breast cancer or does it cause it ? Depends on which study you read .
The latest volley in this battle was fired by researchers from Loma Linda University who concluded that even small amounts of milk , as little as one-third of a cup a day , can significantly raise the risk of breast cancer .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;This was not some haphazard study .
It involved following some 53,000 women who were initially free of breast cancer for eight years .
Food frequency questionnaires were filled out at the beginning of the study , and a smaller contingent also periodically filled out 24 hour recall questionnaires that seemed to validate that the whole cohort did not make major dietary changes over the trial period .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Eventually , 1,057 cases of breast cancer were diagnosed and the likelihood of diagnosis increased with increased milk consumption .
When the numbers were crunched , the researchers concluded that if 100 women who drink no milk would start drinking one-third of a cup a day , about 20 would eventually be diagnosed with cancer .
That is a worrisome statistic .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;The subjects were all Seventh Day Adventists , with a large subset consuming either no dairy or little dairy , thereby providing a significant group for comparison with the milk drinkers .
Soy products were also frequently consumed in this population and were not associated with breast cancer .
Substituting these for milk actually offered protection against the disease .
Cheese and yogurt were not associated with breast cancer .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;The researchers suggested several possible reasons why milk can increase the risk of the disease .
Since the lactating cows are usually pregnant , they secrete estrogen and progesterone in the milk and these may play a role in stimulating cell proliferation .
Milk also contains insulin-like growth factor 1 ( IGF-1 ) , a protein that some studies have implicated as a possible stimulant of cancer cells .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;There is no question that this study was well done .
But -- and there is always a but , is n't there ? -- j&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;ust a few keystrokes can bring up other studies that also seem to be equally well done but come to the opposite conclusion .
In 2015 , Chinese researchers analyzed 22 prospective studies involving over 1 .
million subjects and five case-control studies with a total of 33,000 subjects and found that when the results were pooled , high and modest milk consumption significantly reduced the risk of breast cancer compared with low dairy consumption .
A possible rationale was a protective effect due to calcium .
Then in 2019 , another meta-analysis of case-control studies , published in the journal Medicine , found no association between milk consumption and breast cancer .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;So what do we make of these battling studies ? Basically , that nutritional research , even if well carried out , can not account for all confounders and rarely comes to a conclusion that ca n't be debated .
This is the case not only for dairy consumption , but for such things as artificial sweeteners , saturated fats , dietary supplements , processed meats and organic foods .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;In this instance , the study subjects were Seventh Day Adventists whose lifestyle is significantly different from the general population .
They eat a mostly plant-based diet , shun junk food and drink no alcohol .
Obesity is virtually unknown .
Since both alcohol consumption and obesity are associated with breast cancer , it is possible that elimination of these allows the milk connection to be revealed .
Also , the high milk consumers were likely to also eat more meat and fewer plant products .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Because of possible confounders , no observational study can prove cause and effect .
Still , the Loma Linda study does ring some alarm bells .
It certainly calls into question the wisdom of the common recommendation that consumers drink three glasses of milk a day .
It is also noteworthy that breast cancer rates in Japan have increased significantly with an increase in milk consumption since the Second World War .
Taking everything into account , the link between milk consumption and breast cancer can not be dismissed .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;em&gt;Joe Schwarcz is director of McGill University 's Office for Science &amp; Society ( mcgill .
&lt;/em&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;31486;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;31528;TOOLONG .
by Joe **29;31563;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Joe Schwarcz , Special to the Montreal GazetteMon , 02 Mar 2020 21:13:24 **45;31594;TOOLONG .
Treat those aching knees and hips with exercisehttp : **32;31641;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;31675;TOOLONG .
title= " Evidence shows mind-body/flexibility exercises such as yoga are among the most effective at decreasing joint pain and improving joint function .
" alt= " Evidence shows mind-body/flexibility exercises such as yoga are among the most effective at decreasing joint pain and improving joint function .
" data-portal-copyright= " John Mahoney " **28;31710;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1731448 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; If you&amp;rsquo ; re of a certain age , you probably know all about the aches and pains of osteoarthritis .
A progressive disease found most often in the hips , knees , hands and spine , osteoarthritis is characterized by joint stiffness and pain caused by the breakdown of cartilage and bone in the joint .
Felt largely by the over-50 crowd , it&amp;rsquo ; s been linked to the wear and tear associated with living an active life .
Yet there&amp;rsquo ; s little science to suggest a lifelong love of exercise will lead to sore knees and hips .
In fact , exercise is considered a valuable part of any treatment plan designed to relieve pain and improve the function of affected joints .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; As important as exercise is in managing osteoarthritis , there&amp;rsquo ; s no universal prescription guaranteed to make aching joints feel and move better .
So while it&amp;rsquo ; s clear that some exercise is better than no exercise , opinion varies as to whether hitting the pool , gym , track , bike or yoga mat is the best option .
Of course , that doesn&amp;rsquo ; t stop friends , neighbours , co-workers and even physicians from sharing their view on the type of exercise they feel will make the pain go away , including suggesting that you give up the activities you love in favour of those you don&amp;rsquo ; t .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Understanding that individual experiences shouldn&amp;rsquo ; t be mistaken for a universal truth , a team of researchers reviewed 103 published studies , featuring the results of 9,134 study subjects , on the effectiveness of different types of exercise on improving pain and function in osteoarthritic hips and knees .
The studies were separated into groups depending on the type of exercise used in the protocol &amp;mdash ; aerobic exercise ( swimming , running , cycling ) , strength training ( body weight or weight training exercises ) , mind-body/flexibility exercises ( yoga , Pilates ) and mixed exercise ( more than one type performed in a single workout ) &amp;mdash ; and evaluated on how effective they were in reducing pain and improving function and quality of life .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Assessing benchmarks from the start of a regular exercise routine to eight weeks later , all of the exercise protocols demonstrated a positive effect on joint function and pain compared to the non-exercise controls .
But when comparing one type of exercise to another , aerobic exercise and mind-body exercise proved the most effective at decreasing joint pain and improving joint function .
Less effective was strength training , with mixed exercise providing the least amount of positive benefit .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Why do some types of exercise work better than others at making knees and hips feel 10 years younger ? The researchers have a hunch .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Although the underlying mechanism remains unclear , the effect of both aerobic and mind-body exercise may be attributable to the potential of these exercises to influence altered central elements such as central pain sensitization , sleep disturbance and mood disorders , &amp;rdquo ; they said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Whether there&amp;rsquo ; s enough science to rule out any one type of exercise from the spectrum of options prescribed to reduce osteoarthritis pain is questionable .
But what&amp;rsquo ; s interesting about this review is the lack of effectiveness of mixed exercise .
Given the limited amount of detail regarding the mixed exercise routines included in the studies , it&amp;rsquo ; s difficult to state unequivocally that workouts like &lt;a href= " https : **33;31740;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;HIIT ( high-intensity interval training ) &lt;/a&gt; or &lt;a href= " https : **33;31775;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;CrossFit&lt;/a&gt; are ineffective at making osteoarthritic joints move and feel better .
Combined with the fact that exercise adherence is linked to exercise enjoyment , giving up your favourite mixed routine in favour of aerobic or mind-body options isn&amp;rsquo ; t necessary .
But if you&amp;rsquo ; re unhappy with the results of your workout , adding a few more aerobic workouts or yoga classes to your routine might be worth the effort .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; On the plus side , it&amp;rsquo ; s clear that staying physically active improves joint health .
That&amp;rsquo ; s great news for exercise junkies who have been told to rest their aching joints , or for those who have been advised to give up their favourite aerobic activity in favour of something less stressful on the joints .
Still , you need to pay attention to your body and what makes exercise tick for you , even in the face of growing evidence that some types of exercise are better for your aching joints than others .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; If you&amp;rsquo ; re always sore after an aerobic workout , try yoga .
If yoga or strength training makes your joints ache , hop on a bike .
Ideally , your preferred exercise routine dulls joint pain and improves joint function , which means greater range of motion and less stiffness in the morning .
Given that all forms of exercise are osteoarthritis-friendly when compared to no exercise at all , there&amp;rsquo ; s no shortage of options .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; One final caveat : give your joints time to get used to a new form of exercise before discarding it as ineffective .
Sometimes a little discomfort arrives ahead of relief , so be patient .
That said , pain is different than discomfort , so don&amp;rsquo ; t ignore your body&amp;rsquo ; s red flags .
The end goal is not only finding an exercise routine that helps your joints move more and hurt less , but one you&amp;rsquo ; ll stick with for more than eight weeks .

" alt= " It 's not spring yet .
A skater makes the turn at the end of the frozen lake at the Laval Nature Centre .
" data-portal-copyright= " John Mahoney " **28;32889;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1727448 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; If you&amp;rsquo ; ve ever yelled &amp;ldquo ; This house is a circus ! &amp;rdquo ; , you&amp;rsquo ; re probably a parent .

contortion , sometimes we forget the circus is meant to be full of magic and joy .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The rich history of the circus &amp;mdash ; the kind in tents with three rings , not the kind with laundry &amp;mdash ; is being celebrated by Tohu and the Acc&amp;egrave ; s Culture network from Feb .

" data-portal-copyright= " " **28;34348;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1727801 " /&gt; &lt;h3&gt;How to survive bringing your child to the office&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; Sometimes things happen and you have no choice but to bring your child to work , assuming you work in an office environment and not , say , construction .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The days of children being seen but not heard are over , if they indeed ever existed .
Here are a few tips to help ensure an office visit turns out OK .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;bull ; No one likes surprises , least of all your child and your boss .
Speak to them both beforehand , discussing expectations , rules and an exit plan .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;bull ; Bring lots of books , but if you have a pre-reader , think about how much time you&amp;rsquo ; ll have to read One Fish Two Fish over and over .
If ever there was a &lt;a href= " http : **34;34378;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;time and place for a screen&lt;/a&gt; , this might be it .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;bull ; Find out if anyone else at the office is having the same problem .
Arrange to sit your kids near each other and to share duties checking in on them .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;bull ; Do not let kids mess with anyone else&amp;rsquo ; s workspace .
It&amp;rsquo ; s fun to check out the pictures of Peter&amp;rsquo ; s kids and the dinosaurs on Anne&amp;rsquo ; s desk , but don&amp;rsquo ; t touch .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;bull ; Give your kid a job .
They&amp;rsquo ; ll be happier , at least for a few minutes , to be mirroring what you&amp;rsquo ; re doing .
Younger kids can jab away at a spare keyboard ; older kids might be put to use filing or alphabetizing .
Short assignments will help the day go by more quickly .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;bull ; If they have a meltdown &amp;mdash ; and who doesn&amp;rsquo ; t have an office meltdown now and again ? &amp;mdash ; see Point 1 re : exit plan .
Even if your family rules dictate not responding to tantrums , take it into the hallway , bathroom or outside as fast as possible .
Your colleagues ( especially the ones who aren&amp;rsquo ; t parents ) will appreciate it .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;bull ; Stay calm .
It&amp;rsquo ; s not easy for the kid either .
Check in with them often .

" &gt;Hanes : Panic does n't help , but latest coronavirus news is **31;35072;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Montreal GazetteThu , 27 Feb 2020 12:50:37 **45;35105;TOOLONG .
Labos : We still prescribe too many antibioticshttp : **29;35152;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;35183;TOOLONG .
title= " A pharmacy manager counts out the correct number of antibiotic pills to fill a prescription .
" If nearly half of the antibiotics we prescribe and take are unjustified , then we have a lot of room for improvement , " Christopher Labos writes .
" alt= " A pharmacy manager counts out the correct number of antibiotic pills to fill a prescription .
" If nearly half of the antibiotics we prescribe and take are unjustified , then we have a lot of room for improvement , " Christopher Labos writes .
" data-portal-copyright= " Joe Raedle " **28;35218;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1730297 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; It probably won&amp;rsquo ; t be the coronavirus that does us in as a species .
It probably won&amp;rsquo ; t be Ebola , either .
If there&amp;rsquo ; s one infectious disease issue that we need to worry about , it&amp;rsquo ; s &lt;a href= " https : **33;35248;TOOLONG .
resistance .
&lt;/a&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s a growing problem and it&amp;rsquo ; s happening because we prescribe too many antibiotics .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Antibiotic resistance is listed by the World Health Organization as one of the &lt;a href= " https : **33;35283;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;top 10 threats to global health , &lt;/a&gt; and with good reason .
Antibiotics have prevented untold numbers of deaths since penicillin was first used clinically in the 1940s .
Penicillin use during the Second World War saved many soldiers from a battlefield death caused by infected wounds .
But with time and use , bacteria become resistant to existing antibiotics , which then forces medical researchers to develop new antibiotics to replace them .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; While investing in research to produce new antibiotics is always going to be necessary , we can slow the process of resistance down considerably by limiting the amount of antibiotics we prescribe .
This idea , called antibiotic stewardship , is becoming increasingly important .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Unfortunately , we appear to be prescribing antibiotics at high volumes and often for no good reason .
A recent paper in the &lt;a href= " https : **33;35318;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;British Medical Journal&lt;/a&gt; analyzed data from the National Ambulatory Medical Care Survey .
Of the 991 million doctor&amp;rsquo ; s office visits that occurred in the United States in 2015 , about 130 million resulted in an antibiotic prescription .
What was worrisome in their analysis is that only around half ( 57 per cent ) of antibiotic prescriptions had an appropriate reason for the prescription documented in the patient&amp;rsquo ; s chart .
The remaining 43 per cent either had no reason documented or were given antibiotics for inappropriate indications like for the common cold .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; When we talk about overprescribing antibiotics , we typically think of antibiotics being handed out to children with mild viral illness .
On average , children have between &lt;a href= " https : **33;35353;TOOLONG .
and seven colds per year&lt;/a&gt; and a common refrain is that physicians and parents should not turn to antibiotics for the common cold , which is after all a viral illness that will not respond to antibiotics .
And yet this research shows that adults , particularly adult males , were more likely to get antibiotics than children , which runs counter to the usual assumptions .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Another big factor in whether patients got inappropriate antibiotics or not was whether patients were seeing their regular GP or some other physician .
Patients who saw their regular GP were much less likely to get antibiotics .
Presumably , if you go see a doctor who is unfamiliar with your medical history they would be more likely to prescribe antibiotics just to &amp;ldquo ; be safe .
&amp;rdquo ; And while this might be understandable , it is clearly sub-optimal .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; These types of studies are important because we need to identify factors that lead to unnecessary antibiotics .
One of the biggest hurdles has thankfully already been addressed .
For many years , low-dose antibiotics were given to livestock as a growth supplement and were available over the counter without a prescription .
In fact , some estimates suggested that about &lt;a href= " https : **33;35388;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;80 per cent of the antibiotics we use&lt;/a&gt; were actually used in animals , not in people .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; This changed in December 2018 , when &lt;a href= " https : **33;35423;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;new rules&lt;/a&gt; were put into effect restricting the sales of antibiotics for animals unless you had a prescription from a vet .
So while you could still get antibiotics for your livestock if they were sick , the days of feeding animals antibiotics to make them grow faster are essentially over .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Reducing antibiotic use is an important ( but not the only ) part of combating antibiotic resistance .
If nearly half of the antibiotics we prescribe and take are unjustified , then we have a lot of room for improvement .
We have taken significant steps in Canada to limit unnecessary antibiotic use in animals .
Now we just need to do it in people .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;em&gt;Christopher Labos&lt;/em&gt; &lt;em&gt; is a Montreal doctor and an associate with the McGill Office for Science and Society .
He also co-hosts a podcast called The Body of Evidence .
&lt;/em&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;35458;TOOLONG .
