&lt;/p&gt; Montreal GazetteWed , 19 Feb 2020 22:33:11 **45;35746;TOOLONG .
Snow-removal fury ? Smiling Philippe Sabourin is here to helphttp : **36;35793;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;35831;TOOLONG .
title= " Montreal spokesperson Philippe Sabourin shows off the monitoring centre where over 500 cameras keep a watch over the road network in Montreal , on Thursday , February 13 , 2020 .
" alt= " Montreal spokesperson Philippe Sabourin shows off the monitoring centre where over 500 cameras keep a watch over the road network in Montreal , on Thursday , February 13 , 2020 .
" data-portal-copyright= " Allen McInnis " **28;35866;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1722899 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;35896;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; Why is this man always smiling ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; He spends much of his days and nights often getting peppered by the press about slow snow removal and slippery streets and sidewalks sometimes perceived to be less pristine than bike paths .
Not to mention criticism about rampant street construction , broken water pipes , mobility or lack thereof , recycling , composting and , natch , the ever-ongoing Mountain road imbroglio .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Such is the life of city of Montreal spokesperson Philippe Sabourin .
He is on the front line &amp;mdash ; some might even say the firing line &amp;mdash ; in seeking to explain city-hall decisions that some find confounding .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Sabourin awakes around 4:30 a .
to see what&amp;rsquo ; s up or down in the city .
He can often be heard on radio at 6 a .
and then on the tube throughout the day .
He can be counted on to send text messages to media up until late at night .
In short , he&amp;rsquo ; s always available .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; This is a job that could give most ulcers .
Not Sabourin .
He relishes it all .
He&amp;rsquo ; s not just a glass-half-full fellow &amp;mdash ; his mug overflows .
I suspect he may even whistle while he works .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; There&amp;rsquo ; s no stress here for me .
I honestly love what I do , and so I remain positive all the time , &amp;rdquo ; says the ever-affable Sabourin , 47 , &amp;nbsp ; who became the city&amp;rsquo ; s spokesperson three years ago .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; I&amp;rsquo ; m confident because I feel I have the information to understand the situation and make citizens more aware of the challenges we face .
And they are more willing to accept the situation , even if it&amp;rsquo ; s difficult .
They understand there&amp;rsquo ; s no way we can get rid of two-metre-high snowbanks in just a few days .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The stats appear to support Sabourin&amp;rsquo ; s assertion .
Despite frequent media outrage over these issues &amp;mdash ; &lt;a href= " https : **33;35932;TOOLONG .
plead guilty here&lt;/a&gt; &amp;mdash ; citizen complaints have dropped .
Between Nov .
1 and Feb .
10 , the city received 397 from the 19 boroughs .
That&amp;rsquo ; s down considerably from last year&amp;rsquo ; s 707 complaints over the same period .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Sabourin is taking me and Montreal Gazette photographer Allen McInnis on a drive through the city to check out key operational posts on the snow-battle front .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Since Feb .
6 , Montreal has received about 60 centimetres of snow and , as of Sunday , the cleanup was 95 per cent completed .
Sabourin estimates the job will be finished by Monday &amp;mdash ; unless another storm strikes .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; But even on a relatively calm day , Sabourin is having to deal with complaints from LaSalle residents about unplowed sidewalks and from irate city motorists who&amp;rsquo ; ve been issued tickets on streets after they&amp;rsquo ; ve been cleaned , but with the No Parking signs still erroneously in place .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; In the first instance , the problem relates to massive amounts of snow removed from homes and driveways , thus requiring heavier artillery to clear sidewalks .
And while sympathetic to the plight of wrongly ticketed motorists , Sabourin notes this is more a police issue .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Then there&amp;rsquo ; s the reality of some boroughs being faster than others in removal operations .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s like we&amp;rsquo ; re running a marathon here .
It doesn&amp;rsquo ; t always matter who is fastest , but more that we all get to the finish line in good time .
Often , we have to work on steeper hills first , as is the case in the Ville-Marie borough .
In &amp;Icirc ; le-Bizard , it&amp;rsquo ; s fast , because they don&amp;rsquo ; t have to transport the snow .
They can blow it on the side .
But in C&amp;ocirc ; te-des-Neiges , they have to load the snow at night , because there&amp;rsquo ; s so much traffic during the day and they&amp;rsquo ; re so far away from the land dump sites .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; What has to be considered is the geographic situation of each borough in relation to the dump sites and the density of the population .
Each borough has to figure out the best strategy .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Sabourin disputes a conspiracy theory about bike paths receiving priority treatment .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The point is we use different tools and machinery for the streets , sidewalks and bike paths .
They all start working around the same time but there&amp;rsquo ; s certainly no bike-path priority .
We try to do sidewalks first to ensure pedestrian safety .
We realize it&amp;rsquo ; s not perfect , but we are trying .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The city is a network of 10,000 kilometres , 6,000 of which are sidewalks and only 700 of which are bike paths .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; That&amp;rsquo ; s the equivalent of the distance between Montreal and James Bay , &amp;rdquo ; Sabourin says .
&amp;ldquo ; That&amp;rsquo ; s our challenge , and clearing it is like a military operation .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; That would make executive committee member and Verdun mayor Jean-Fran&amp;ccedil ; ois Parenteau the general .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Over 3,000 workers are involved in this operation .
The cost is equally enormous , about $1 million per every cleared centimetre of snowfall , according to Sabourin .
While we&amp;rsquo ; ve already received close to the seasonal average of 190 centimetres , only 120 centimetres has had to be cleared away .
The rest has melted on its own .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The snow-removal budget this winter is about $180 million , but should we get blasted again , there&amp;rsquo ; s still plenty of capacity left to accommodate it at the city&amp;rsquo ; s 12 land and 16 sewer dump sites , which together can handle up to 18 million cubic metres of snow .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;img src= " https : **33;35967;TOOLONG .
title= " A contracted dump truck operator unloads into the sewer system at one of the approved sewer dumps in Montreal on Thursday , Feb .
13 , 2020 .
The sewer dump is located under the Jacques Cartier Bridge and feeds in to one of the largest sewers in the city , which transports the melts snow to the water-filtration plant in east-end Montreal .
" alt= " A contracted dump truck operator unloads into the sewer system at one of the approved sewer dumps in Montreal on Thursday , Feb .
13 , 2020 .
The sewer dump is located under the Jacques Cartier Bridge and feeds in to one of the largest sewers in the city , which transports the melts snow to the water-filtration plant in east-end Montreal .
" data-portal-copyright= " Allen McInnis " **28;36002;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1723972 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; On the subject of sewer sites , we visit one under the Jacques-Cartier Bridge .
During the height of snow-removal operations , 100 trucks an hour , 24/7 , drop off their loads here .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Sabourin explains that the sewer sites save a lot of time , especially in the downtown area , where trucks don&amp;rsquo ; t have to haul snow at land sites farther away .
He also is quick to point out that the dumped snow goes through a water treatment process before being moved into the St-Lawrence River .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; In the old days , the snow , which can contain salt and grease , went straight into the river , without regard to the environment , &amp;rdquo ; Sabourin says .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; We also visit &amp;ldquo ; command central , &amp;rdquo ; a small office in an Old Montreal highrise .
Staff here monitors road conditions on 550 closed-circuit cameras throughout the city .
Based on their surveillance , they are able to direct crews from affected boroughs to trouble spots .
They also control traffic lights , in case of emergencies .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; The worst scenario is freezing rain and ice pellets , especially in hilly areas , &amp;rdquo ; Sabourin says .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Adds staffer Alain Dupuis : &amp;ldquo ; We see everything that goes on in the city here , and some of it can be pretty crazy .
But the key is not to panic .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; That appears to be the prerequisite for a job here .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; I love the snow .
It&amp;rsquo ; s like a winter wonderland for me here .
That explains why I&amp;rsquo ; m so positive , &amp;rdquo ; Sabourin says .
&amp;ldquo ; There&amp;rsquo ; s little more beautiful a sight than watching one of our machines at a land site blowing snow 140 feet in the air at sunrise .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Such a romantic .
But surely there must be a downside to the job .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; What&amp;rsquo ; s Philippe doing between the tempests ? Why , he&amp;rsquo ; s dealing with the potholes , &amp;rdquo ; Sabourin says with a sigh .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Plus &amp;ccedil ; a change &amp;hellip ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " **32;36032;TOOLONG " target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **39;36066;TOOLONG &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " https : **28;36107;TOOLONG " target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **30;36137;TOOLONG &; .

more of Bill Brownstein 's recent columns right **25;36281;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Bill Brownstein , Montreal GazetteMon , 17 Feb 2020 11:00:09 **45;36308;TOOLONG .
NewsBrownstein : Area-code overload dials up the anxietyhttp : **33;36355;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;36390;TOOLONG .
title= " What would Lily Tomlin 's iconic phone-operator character Ernestine have to say about the exhaustion and proliferation of area codes .
Too many ringy-dingies ! " alt= " What would Lily Tomlin 's iconic phone-operator character Ernestine have to say about the exhaustion and proliferation of area codes .
Too many ringy-dingies ! " data-portal-copyright= " " **28;36425;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1715804 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; Are your brains already addled with way too many digits running through them ? Wait , it&amp;rsquo ; s going to get worse as we&amp;rsquo ; ll soon be inundated with yet more area codes to scramble our heads .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; In old-timey times &amp;mdash ; before there were cellular phones and that internet thingy &amp;mdash ; most mere mortals had to memorize only a few digits and a couple of letters , generally relating to telephone numbers .
It wasn&amp;rsquo ; t much of an issue .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; In those days , it would have been unthinkable to have to remember one area code along with a seven-digit number , which was the norm up until not long ago .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; But little could we have known just what kind of pressure was to be placed on our beleaguered hippocampi this century as the numbers to be recalled keep rolling out at frightening speed .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; According to our elders , humans in the middle part of the last century only had to keep track of two letters and four numbers , then five numbers , before giving their fingers a workout on a now antique contraption called a rotary phone .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The letters referred to the first two in names like Crescent , Dollard , Regent , Wellington .
Then one had to have the faculties to match those letters with the appropriate numbers on the rotary , before following with the four or five numbers .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Pretty simple stuff , as long as the finger dexterity was there .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It was even simpler before , according to the elders of our elders , when one just had to remember &amp;lsquo ; 0 , &amp;rsquo ; which signified the operator , often called Mabel , who upon a caller dialing or cranking up an antique phone gizmo would connect one to the police or your neighbours &amp;mdash ; all while listening in to the call .
( &lt;a href= " https : **25;36455;TOOLONG ? search .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Search YouTube for videos of Lily Tomlin 's ever-snorting operator Ernestine&lt;/a&gt; , from her days on TV&amp;rsquo ; s Laugh-In , for hysterical insights .
) &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Before that , one had to use Morse code or carrier pigeons to get messages through to the cops or neighbours .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; But life got really tricky , even for the non-numerically memory-challenged , this millennium .
Montrealers had to add 514 to the requisite seven digits for calling within the area .
Tough yet do-able .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Then in 2006 , another code , 438 , was created for the Montreal area , because 514 just wasn&amp;rsquo ; t large enough to handle the volume of new numbers .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Oh yeah , and then there was the 450 code for those in the outlying &amp;lsquo ; burbs , later to be joined by 579 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; And should you have been lucky enough to have family members and friends in the western part of the province , you not only had to remember the 819 code but also 873 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Could it possibly get more complex ? Yes , it could .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Get ready for yet another Montreal code , 263 .
Really ! &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; According to the &lt;a href= " https : **33;36482;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;Canadian Radio-television and Telecommunications Commission ( CRTC ) &lt;/a&gt; , the &lt;a href= " https : **33;36517;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;current projected exhaust date for codes 514 and 438 is June 2024&lt;/a&gt; .
So the Relief Planning Committee ( RPC ) is filing recommendations with the CRTC &amp;mdash ; just remembering all these government acronyms is a challenge &amp;mdash ; on the &amp;ldquo ; suitability&amp;rdquo ; of 263 for relief of the soon-to-be exhausted 514 and 438 and on when 263 should be pressed into service .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Similarly , those in the bloated 450 and 579 areas could soon be welcoming 354 .
And those in the 819 and 873 region , say hey to 468 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; And don&amp;rsquo ; t even ask about Toronto or New York codes .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The mathematics are way beyond my pay grade , but the bottom line is 514 and 438 are maxed out , thanks in large part to the proliferation of smartphones .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Back in those old-timey times , most folks had only one number , but today many families have one landline and several mobiles for its various members .
According to the CRTC , there were 33 .
million Canadian mobile subscribers in 2018 , up 4 .
per cent from 2017 .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Leaving aside the area codes , remembering just the seven-digit numbers of family and friends today can be nightmarish , unless one stores one&amp;rsquo ; s contacts in the recesses of one&amp;rsquo ; s cell .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Of course , it is much more of a nightmare remembering all one&amp;rsquo ; s passwords for everything from email to ATMs , fridges to Facebook .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; According to the biometrics company Veridium , millions of American workers have to remember 27 different passwords , many of which are forgotten after Christmas breaks .
This &amp;ldquo ; password fatigue&amp;rdquo ; can be quite expensive , costing companies US$70 per individual password reset .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Could this result one day in the death of the password , replaced by eye or finger scans ? That might be sweet , although I&amp;rsquo ; ve seen one too many horror flicks where forces of evil have non-surgically extracted eyes and fingers to gain access to their owners&amp;rsquo ; computers and bank accounts .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Regardless , such technology will never help on the 10-digit telephone-number front .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Where&amp;rsquo ; s Mabel when we need her ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " **32;36552;TOOLONG " **39;36586;TOOLONG &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " https : **28;36627;TOOLONG " target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **30;36657;TOOLONG &; .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;36689;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;36731;TOOLONG .
take it easy on us&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;36766;TOOLONG .
recent columns by Bill **31;36801;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; Bill Brownstein , Montreal GazetteWed , 12 Feb 2020 11:00:40 **45;36834;TOOLONG .
NewsNewsOpinionPersonal **25;36881;TOOLONG Labos : A surgical mask wo n't protect you from coronavirushttp : **29;36908;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;36939;TOOLONG .
title= " People line up to buy protective face masks amid concerns of the novel coronavirus outbreak that originated in central China , outside a shop in Hanoi on February 10 , 2020 .
" alt= " People line up to buy protective face masks amid concerns of the novel coronavirus outbreak that originated in central China , outside a shop in Hanoi on February 10 , 2020 .
" data-portal-copyright= " NHAC NGUYEN " **28;36974;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1719677 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **32;37004;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; The following is a public service announcement : Please stop stealing masks from your doctor&amp;rsquo ; s office .
I realize that people are worried about coronavirus , but before you commit petty theft , you should probably know that those masks won&amp;rsquo ; t protect you from catching the virus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; On the off chance that you haven&amp;rsquo ; t heard , the coronavirus has been declared a &lt;a href= " https : **33;37038;TOOLONG .
health emergency&lt;/a&gt; by the World Health Organization .
To date , it has &lt;a href= " http : **34;37073;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;infected&lt;/a&gt; more than 28,000 people and caused 565 deaths worldwide .
To put this in perspective , the &lt;a href= " https : **33;37109;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;flu&lt;/a&gt; has infected 22 million and killed some 12,000 people during this flu season in the United States alone , which makes it a much more dangerous virus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Still , the coronavirus outbreak does pose a risk if not properly handled .
It was , after all , a coronavirus strain that caused the SARS outbreak of 2002 and the MERS outbreak in the Middle East in 2012 .
For those who knew people in Toronto during SARS , especially for those who had friends in the health care field who got sick , the memory of that episode is still fresh .
But surgical masks are not going to help .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Many doctors&amp;rsquo ; offices have boxes of surgical masks laid out at reception for patients who come in with symptoms like sneezing or coughing .
These are provided so that sick patients will not spread their germs to others in the waiting room .
But colleagues of mine have told me that some patients are leaving with fistfuls of surgical masks or simply taking the box altogether .
The result has been a &lt;a href= " https : **33;37144;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;global shortage of masks&lt;/a&gt; .
The other day , I went to the pharmacy , and as I walked in the door the clerk told me that they were out of surgical masks and would probably not get more anytime soon .
I told them that I just came in to buy some shampoo .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; There are several problems with this run on masks .
First , stealing is wrong .
But more important , the regular surgical masks that some people seem to be hoarding won&amp;rsquo ; t actually protect you from coronavirus .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Most common infections are spread via droplets .
In other words , every time you cough or sneeze when sick , tiny water droplets that contain virus particles are sprayed around you .
These can directly infect someone close by , or can land on a nearby surface like a table or a chair .
Someone might then touch that table and put their hand to the eyes , nose or mouth and thus transmit the virus to themselves .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The problem with standard surgical masks is that they are not airtight seals around your mouth and nose .
Someone can still cough on you , and infect you or you can still touch contaminated surfaces and infect yourself .
People often ask why doctors are often seen wearing surgical masks throughout the hospital .
The answer is that the masks are designed to prevent you from infecting someone else with your germs , not to prevent someone else&amp;rsquo ; s germs from infecting you .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; If a doctor wanted to protect themselves from an airborne infection , they wouldn&amp;rsquo ; t wear a surgical mask .
They would wear an N95 mask .
The N95 mask actually provides good protection against airborne infections , but it has two drawbacks .
To work , it has to be fitted properly to your face .
Second , I can say from personal experience that after about 20 minutes of wearing a N95 masks you start to become lightheaded and feel unwell , likely because you have been rebreathing increasingly stale air .
It&amp;rsquo ; s not the type of thing you can wear for hours .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s understandable that people are scared about coronavirus , but wearing a surgical mask won&amp;rsquo ; t really do much to protect you .
Though given that only seven people &lt;a href= " https : **33;37179;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;in Canada&lt;/a&gt; are infected with coronavirus , you probably don&amp;rsquo ; t need much protection to begin with .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;em&gt;Christopher Labos&lt;/em&gt; &lt;em&gt; is a Montreal doctor and an associate with the McGill Office for Science and Society .
He also co-hosts a podcast called The Body of Evidence .
&lt;/em&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;37214;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;37256;TOOLONG .
columns by Christopher **26;37291;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;37319;TOOLONG .
unprepared for coronavirus outbreak , says Montrealer back from **26;37354;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;37382;TOOLONG .
selects 4 hospitals as potential coronavirus-treatment **28;37417;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Christopher Labos , Special to Montreal GazetteTue , 11 Feb 2020 16:45:13 **45;37447;TOOLONG .
Valentines do not belong in the classrooms of small childrenhttp : **32;37494;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;37528;TOOLONG .
title= " If we have to do the same thing for everyone , it teaches us nothing about love .
We do not love everyone equally .
" alt= " If we have to do the same thing for everyone , it teaches us nothing about love .
We do not love everyone equally .
" data-portal-copyright= " Bryanna Bradley " **28;37563;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1703103 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; Institutionally sponsored romantic love has no business in an elementary school .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Valentine&amp;rsquo ; s Day is not a celebration of friendship .
It&amp;rsquo ; s an indoctrination of future expectations : flowers , candies , cards and other unsustainable waste as proof of life of one&amp;rsquo ; s relationship .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; We struggle to ensure our children understand consent and to empower them to set their own boundaries with respect to relationships , especially as they gain independence .
According to the Quebec Education Ministry , sexuality education in school should enable students to &amp;ldquo ; better understand themselves ; establish emotional relationships that show respect for themselves and others ; develop critical thinking and good judgment .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Yet this one day of the year comes with an all-or-nothing requirement that&amp;rsquo ; s meant to foster inclusion : bring something for everyone or no one at all .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; That means signing their name to an &amp;ldquo ; I like you beary much&amp;rdquo ; card for a kid who might have bullied them .
It means giving a &amp;ldquo ; You&amp;rsquo ; re a purr-fect friend&amp;rdquo ; card to someone who&amp;rsquo ; s snubbed them during a separate activity .
How does &amp;ldquo ; this is the day you must make a card for the kid who pulls your braids&amp;rdquo ; translate into a lesson about love and compassion ? Let&amp;rsquo ; s rename it Turn The Other Cheek Day .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; If we have to do the same thing for everyone , it teaches us nothing about love .
We do not love everyone equally .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Yet , removing the everyone-or-no-one requirement means there&amp;rsquo ; s a child who&amp;rsquo ; s going to have 15 Valentines and another who&amp;rsquo ; s going to have one &amp;mdash ; and it&amp;rsquo ; ll be from the teacher .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Even more troubling are the fundraising events that inevitably accompany the celebration , usually carnations or candy-grams that will be delivered during class time , profiting off the popular kids and leaving the others with a fake smile .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Well , part of learning about love is learning about heartbreak , right ? No , it isn&amp;rsquo ; t .
Not in elementary school .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Are we turning them into little snowflakes who can&amp;rsquo ; t handle disappointment ? Oh , don&amp;rsquo ; t worry , Chad , there&amp;rsquo ; s still soccer and the talent show and spelling bees to keep them from getting too high and mighty .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s not that Valentine&amp;rsquo ; s Day is bad .
It can be whatever a family decides to make of it .
But it doesn&amp;rsquo ; t belong in elementary school .
If schools want to help teach children about compassion and tie it into Valentine&amp;rsquo ; s Day , they should make cards to deliver to a nearby seniors residence .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; As classrooms raise flags of inclusion and school walls are papered in anti-bullying slogans , carrying on traditions that have the potential to isolate a child is irresponsible and borders on cruel .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " **26;37593;TOOLONG " **33;37621;TOOLONG &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " http : //twitter .
" target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **31;37656;TOOLONG &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;37689;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;37731;TOOLONG .
on kids and parenting from Hayley **25;37766;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Hayley Juhl , Montreal GazetteMon , 10 Feb 2020 23:55:01 **45;37793;TOOLONG .
&amp;amp ; ChildParentingFitness : Does your bra support your workout ? http : **32;37840;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;37874;TOOLONG .
title= " Australian researchers who suggest " commercially available sports bras do not meet the unique needs of elite female athletes across the range of sports they participate in .
" " alt= " Australian researchers who suggest " commercially available sports bras do not meet the unique needs of elite female athletes across the range of sports they participate in .
" " data-portal-copyright= " YASUYOSHI CHIBA " **28;37909;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1713190 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s a subject not often discussed around the gym , despite statistics suggesting 44 to 72 per cent of women experience breast pain while exercising .
Also not often the subject of conversation is even more women ( 51 to 79 per cent ) complain of sore breasts around the time of their period .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; To be clear , not all workouts are painful .
Low-impact activities produce less of a bounce factor , which dials down the discomfort .
But for runners , there&amp;rsquo ; s no doubt breasts move significantly with every footfall .
One-third of the 1,397 female runners ( bra cup size AA-J ) polled prior to competing in the 2012 London Marathon reported experiencing breast pain while exercising .
Eight per cent described the pain as distressing , horrible or excruciating .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; For many women who experience pain during exercise , high-impact activities like running , jumping and skipping rope are out of the question simply because the discomfort is too distracting or takes away from the enjoyment of the activity .
Others are forced to modify their workouts in order to minimize the pain .
A survey of 540 elite athletes across 49 different sports reported one-third experience breast pain severe enough to negatively affect performance and/or interfere with their ability to train .
Additional studies suggest pain can cause women to modify their gait and upper body movements to compensate for excessive breast movement .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The incidence and severity of breast pain is more common among large-breasted women , with 51 per cent of women with an F-cup size or larger complaining of discomfort , compared with 24 per cent of women with an A-cup .
Pain is also more prevalent among women who haven&amp;rsquo ; t given birth .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Kristina Ramsay , a Montreal-based fitness enthusiast , says pain is too strong a word to describe what she feels when exercise ramps up the bounce factor .
An avid skier , runner and gym rat , she suggests &amp;ldquo ; discomfort&amp;rdquo ; and &amp;ldquo ; annoyance&amp;rdquo ; better describe her reality .
A D-cup , she relies on a good sports bra to keep her comfortable during high-impact activities .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; She&amp;rsquo ; s not alone .
A sports bra is the most popular solution when it comes to dampening the pain associated with exercise .
And while sports bras have come a long way from the first prototype of two jocks straps sewn together , not just any bra will do .
An &lt;a href= " https : **33;37939;TOOLONG .
research team who studied the consequences of breast pain on performance&lt;/a&gt; recommends all female athletes need to be educated on how to select and correctly fit a sports bra specific to their sport ( take the &lt;a href= " https : **33;37974;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;lululemon sports bra fit quiz&lt;/a&gt; ) .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Easier said than done , says Ramsay , who searches running blogs and product reviews for suggestions on sports bras specifically designed for exercisers who need maximum support .
She&amp;rsquo ; s tried more than her share of models claiming to fit the bill , only to be disappointed when putting them to the test at the gym or while out on a run .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; It&amp;rsquo ; s no fun feeling like you&amp;rsquo ; re going to fall out or being chafed , &amp;rdquo ; she said .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; And then there&amp;rsquo ; s the cost of a good sports bra , which is no small matter .
A quick look at the lineup of most of the popular sports bra retailers and you&amp;rsquo ; ll note bras boasting maximum support are more expensive than bras offering light or medium support .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Ramsay&amp;rsquo ; s current favourite is the &lt;a href= " https : **33;38009;TOOLONG .
Bra&lt;/a&gt; made by Brooks , which she says has all the features experts recommend to ensure a comfortable workout .
The straps are wide and adjustable , the band around the chest thick enough that it doesn&amp;rsquo ; t ride up and the cups encapsulate versus binding the breasts .
But there&amp;rsquo ; s one feature Ramsay says sports bra manufacturers still haven&amp;rsquo ; t got right .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; All that support and they finish the bra with a couple of flimsy hook and eye closures , &amp;rdquo ; she said .
According to Ramsay , hook and eyes aren&amp;rsquo ; t rugged enough to withstand the magnitude of breast movement that occurs during high-impact activities .
Add a little wear and tear and the bra has a tendency to become unhooked just when it&amp;rsquo ; s needed most .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Her experience jives with the sentiments of the Australian researchers who suggest &amp;ldquo ; commercially available sports bras do not meet the unique needs of elite female athletes across the range of sports they participate in .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Given the limitations of sports bras as well as the prevalence of breast pain among elite and recreational athletes , it&amp;rsquo ; s clear the industry hasn&amp;rsquo ; t been successful in meeting the needs of a diverse community of exercisers who look forward to pain-free workouts .
And then there are the differences between sports .
Are runners and equestrians equally well-served in the same bra ? And what about soccer players , who use their chest to control and bring down a ball in flight ; is there a bra to fit their needs ? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; All female exercisers deserve the right to work out pain-free , even on those days when breasts are tender .
Active women also deserve the right not only to wear a bra that stays clasped when the going gets sweaty , but to buy it at the same price as exercisers for whom support isn&amp;rsquo ; t as important .

&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; The woman was about to give birth , her baby&amp;rsquo ; s head crowning through the vaginal opening .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; But the doctor sensed something was dangerously wrong : the baby&amp;rsquo ; s shoulder was being blocked by the woman&amp;rsquo ; s pelvic bone , a condition known as shoulder dystocia that in rare cases can cause a stillbirth .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; In an instant , Dr .
Xingbang Zheng spread the woman&amp;rsquo ; s legs far apart and high into the air as he pressed down on her belly .
Those manoeuvres made the woman&amp;rsquo ; s pelvic bone rotate , allowing the baby&amp;rsquo ; s shoulder to slip through without mishap .
A couple of seconds later , Zheng was holding the infant in his arms &amp;mdash ; or rather , a mannequin designed to look like a baby .

&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The MUHC Foundation aims to raise $10 million to establish the network in one to two years .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; This network is going to create more of a patient-safety culture at our hospitals , &amp;rdquo ; Dr .

&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Ultimately , the patient will benefit .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The Canadian Patient Safety Institute estimates that medical errors account for 28,000 deaths each year in Canada .
Although all physicians undergo residency training and evaluation in hospitals , they need to keep up with their skills .
That&amp;rsquo ; s why medical simulation is so essential .

&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Marc Parent , CAE&amp;rsquo ; s chief executive officer and a member of the MUHC Foundation&amp;rsquo ; s board , said his company is applying the principles of civil aviation safety to health care .

&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " https : **33;38748;TOOLONG .

Richard Cruess&lt;/a&gt; , the former dean of medicine at McGill , is still involved in medical education at the age of 90 , and marvelled at the latest advances in simulation .
Cruess recalled that as a student in the early 1950s , he and his classmates had to sacrifice about 200 rabbits to learn how to suture .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We would inflict wounds of different types on the rabbits as groups of students , &amp;rdquo ; Cruess recounted .
&amp;ldquo ; One student would be the anesthetist and another student would be the surgeon .
In retrospect , it was awful .
It was a different world then .
Patient rights had not really been well established , much less animal rights .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Today , in contrast , &amp;ldquo ; you don&amp;rsquo ; t even think in those terms anymore .
The revolution in technology , which of course includes simulation , is like magic .

from Aaron **27;39151;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Aaron Derfel , Montreal GazetteThu , 06 Feb 2020 12:39:07 **45;39180;TOOLONG .
BusinessLocal NewsFitness : Nine ways to clean up our gym etiquettehttp : **31;39227;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;39260;TOOLONG .
title= " Wiping down machines is n't the only chore you 're expected to perform at the gym .
" alt= " Wiping down machines is n't the only chore you 're expected to perform at the gym .
" data-portal-copyright= " Dave Sidaway " **28;39295;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1707576 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;39325;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s been a few weeks since &lt;a href= " https : **33;39361;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;the New Year , New You crowd&lt;/a&gt; invaded the gym , which means the grace period for poor gym etiquette is drawing to a close .
As accustomed as the old guard is to the annual January flood of exercise newbies , there comes a time when missteps in decorum are no longer forgiven .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; To be fair , most gyms do a lousy job of educating their members on how to foster a safe and welcoming workout space .
A few strategically placed signs outlining one or two basic guidelines is the standard approach , but it&amp;rsquo ; s violations of the unsaid rules that cause eyebrows to raise and words to be exchanged .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; So to clear up any confusion around what&amp;rsquo ; s kosher and what&amp;rsquo ; s not , here are nine rules to live by .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;The gym&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Respect personal space .
&lt;/strong&gt; Most people try to get into the zone during a workout , which means focusing on the job at hand with earbuds in and playlist setting the mood .
Be sure to give your fellow exercise enthusiasts enough space to do their thing and refrain from striking up a conversation , commenting on their form or peeking at their workout stats from a neighbouring treadmill , bike or elliptical .
Above all else , no matter how funky the workout , don&amp;rsquo ; t stare .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Clean up after yourself .
&lt;/strong&gt; Workouts are sweaty endeavours that call for wiping down machines , mats , balls , weights and benches after use &amp;mdash ; particularly during flu season .
But that&amp;rsquo ; s not the only chore you&amp;rsquo ; re expected to perform .
Re-rack your weights , remove the plates from barbells and return any other pieces of equipment to their rightful place .
As for your personal equipment &amp;mdash ; water bottle , towel and any other accoutrements &amp;mdash ; keep it with you , not littered around the gym .
And for everybody&amp;rsquo ; s sake , stay away from the gym if you&amp;rsquo ; re sneezing or coughing .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Leave your phone -- and yourself -- on silent .
&lt;/strong&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s fine to use your phone to play music ( earbuds only , please ) , but not to FaceTime friends and family , text while exercising , take workout selfies or upload pictures of those working out around you to Instagram .
And while you&amp;rsquo ; re keeping your phone out of sight , put it on silent so it doesn&amp;rsquo ; t ring , ping or otherwise disrupt the workout of the person next to you .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Keep it scent-free .
&lt;/strong&gt; Strong scents are particularly annoying at the gym , where respiration rate is ramped up and sweaty bodies are working out side by side .
That&amp;rsquo ; s not an excuse to dial back on the deodorant &amp;mdash ; just avoid flowery or heavy scents that linger .
Speaking of unpleasant smells , don&amp;rsquo ; t make the mistake of squeezing in one more workout before throwing your favourite gym T-shirt , shorts or leggings in the wash .
Nobody likes to exercise beside someone with overripe gear .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Indoor shoes only .
&lt;/strong&gt; Hey , it&amp;rsquo ; s Canada , where snow , salt and other abrasives cling to all outdoor footwear .
And no matter how hard you try to wipe the outdoors away , dirt , grit and moisture get tracked into the gym and locker room , and then transferred to machines and other equipment .
Leave your boots at the door , and don&amp;rsquo ; t make the mistake of thinking you can get from the parking lot to the front door in your gym shoes without bringing the outside in .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Do n't hog the equipment .
&lt;/strong&gt; Gyms are communal spaces , which means equipment is shared , not monopolized .
This is especially relevant during peak hours , when there aren&amp;rsquo ; t enough machines and pieces of equipment to go around .
Limit your time on a cardio machine to 30 minutes , and give a nod to indicate it&amp;rsquo ; s OK for someone to use the weight training equipment when you&amp;rsquo ; re between sets .
Just make sure you put a towel down on the weight bench so you&amp;rsquo ; re not sharing more than a set of dumbbells .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;The locker room&lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Cover up .
&lt;/strong&gt; You may be comfortable in your birthday suit , but not everyone is cool with people walking around in the buff .
That doesn&amp;rsquo ; t mean you can&amp;rsquo ; t expose any bare skin , but throw on a towel while heading to and from the shower .
And remember the rule about personal space , making sure not to spread your discarded workout clothes and toiletries around the locker room like it&amp;rsquo ; s your own bathroom .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Cover your feet , too .
&lt;/strong&gt; Locker rooms and showers are breeding grounds for germs .
Even the best clubs struggle to keep up the cleanliness of showers , toilet stalls and floors during peak hours .
Opt for flip-flops or slides instead of bare feet , and that includes in the shower .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;strong&gt;Get in and get out .
&lt;/strong&gt; Locker rooms aren&amp;rsquo ; t the place to loiter , catch up with a buddy , talk on the phone or grab a quick bite to eat .
Nor are they a place to take selfies : understandably , cameras make people nervous when they&amp;rsquo ; re used in a locker room .
And gawking is never cool .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;39396;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;39438;TOOLONG .
from Jill **27;39473;TOOLONG &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;39502;TOOLONG .
' load management ' really a thing in sport ? &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;39537;TOOLONG .
it worth feeling the burn of HIIT ? &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt; &lt;/ul&gt; Jill Barker , Special to Montreal GazetteSun , 02 Feb 2020 18:04:23 **45;39572;TOOLONG &amp;amp ; FitnessHealthLifeLocal NewsThe Right Chemistry : Intermittent fasting is hard .
But does it work ? http : **35;39619;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;39656;TOOLONG .
title= " There is accumulating evidence that calorie restriction provides benefits beyond the obvious weight loss .
" alt= " There is accumulating evidence that calorie restriction provides benefits beyond the obvious weight loss .
" data-portal-copyright= " " **28;39691;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1706345 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;39721;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;The New England Journal of Medicine is widely regarded as perhaps the most prestigious medical journal in the world .
It has an acceptance rate of five per cent , meaning that only one in 20 articles submitted is judged by experts to be worthy of publication .
That does n't mean the rejected papers are not based on sound research ; most eventually get published in lesser journals .
But the New England Journal looks for the cream of the crop .
That 's why I pay particular attention to papers published in this journal , such as a recent article on the &lt;a href= " https : **33;39757;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt; " Effects of Intermittent Fasting on Health , Aging , and Disease .
" &lt;/a&gt; Even more so when the article is the work of Johns Hopkins University neuroscientist Dr .
Mark Mattson , renowned globally for his research in the area of intermittent fasting .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Intermittent fasting does not mean cutting out a Snickers bar between meals .
It refers to a systematic eating pattern that places emphasis not on what food should be eaten , but rather on when it should be consumed .
Intermittent fasts fall into three general categories .
In " alternate day fasting , " days of very low-calorie intake are alternated with days of regular eating .
The " 5:2 " variety dictates eating normally on five days of the week but restricting calories to under 700 on two non-sequential days .
In " daily time-restricted feeding , " all food is consumed in a six-to-eight-hour window , essentially resulting in a 16- to 18-hour fast .
Most people who engage in this version finish supper by about 7 p .
and do not eat again until lunch the next day .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Of course , the question is why anyone would want to engage in any of these torturous regimes .
Simply put , it is because there is accumulating evidence that calorie restriction provides benefits beyond the obvious weight loss .
It has long been known that reduced food intake in animals results in an increased life span .
The assumption has been that the benefits of reduced calorie intake are due to a reduction in the generation of free radicals as a consequence of metabolic processes .
However , it appears that there is another factor involved .
Typically , in experiments in which rodents are put on a low-calorie diet , they are given their daily allotment of food in one dose that they generally consume within a few hours .
This means that essentially , they are on a 20-hour fast .
This results in " metabolic switching , " a term with which we have to become familiar to understand the benefits that are attributed to intermittent fasting .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;The main source of energy for cells is glucose .
During respiration , glucose serves as fuel , providing energy as it reacts with oxygen to yield carbon dioxide and water .
It is this process that is also accompanied by the production of those troublesome free radicals .
The main source of glucose are carbohydrates in the diet and when these are severely restricted , as in fasting , the body switches to fats as an alternate fuel .
But fats are not used directly , they are converted in the liver to " ketone bodies " that then are metabolized yielding energy .
This is commonly referred to as a state of " ketosis .
" &lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;It turns out that these ketones are not just fuel for cells , but are also signalling molecules that regulate the expression and activity of various proteins and other biochemicals that influence health and aging .
It seems that metabolic switching , which is a result of periods of fasting , is perceived by the body as a signal to go into survival mode since no food is coming in .
Cells respond by improving control of blood pressure and blood sugar , producing more antioxidants and curbing inflammation .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Most of the fasting studies that have produced promising results have involved animals , but some human trials are starting to emerge .
Improvements in insulin sensitivity , verbal memory , resting heart rate , and cholesterol levels have been noted in short-term clinical trials .
In rodents , experiments have shown reduced occurrence of spontaneous tumours with daily calorie restriction or alternate-day fasting .
Suppression of the growth of induced tumours has also been observed .
Furthermore , the animals show increased sensitivity to radiation and chemotherapy .
Stimulated by these observations , a number of human trials examining the effect of intermittent fasting on breast , ovarian , prostate , endometrial , colorectal and brain tumours are underway .
Pilot studies are also examining possible benefits of intermittent fasting in multiple sclerosis , rheumatoid arthritis , surgical outcomes and athletic performance .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;Obviously , we have to temper this discussion with the all-too-often-stated disclaimer that more research is needed .
But it is forthcoming .
Valter Longo at the University of Southern California has some interesting results with his " Fasting Mimicking Diet .
" For five days , people consume only special prepackaged foods that provide 1,000 calories the first day and 725 the other days and are said to have a unique combination of nutrients that trick the body into thinking it is fasting .
Repeating the cycle monthly for three months has resulted in weight loss as well as a drop in blood sugar and cholesterol .
But going hungry for five days is challenging and the meals are expensive .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;span class= " s1 " &gt;It is always meaningful to ask experts what change they have made in their life as a result of their research .
Mattson says he eats within a six-hour window every day .
And that 's from the horse 's mouth .
&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " **29;39792;TOOLONG " target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **36;39823;TOOLONG &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;em&gt;Joe Schwarcz is director of McGill University 's Office for Science &amp; Society ( mcgill .
He hosts The Dr .
Joe Show on CJAD Radio 800 AM every Sunday from 3 to 4 p .
&lt;/em&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;39861;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;39903;TOOLONG .
columns by Joe **29;39938;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Joe Schwarcz , Special to the Montreal GazetteFri , 31 Jan 2020 18:52:45 **45;39969;TOOLONG .
&amp;amp ; **38;40016;TOOLONG Labos : Is there a cancer risk with talcum powder ? http : **33;40056;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;40091;TOOLONG .
title= " Johnson &amp; Johnson has lost a string of lawsuits with the biggest ordering a payout of $4 .
billion .
" alt= " Johnson &amp; Johnson has lost a string of lawsuits with the biggest ordering a payout of $4 .
billion .
" data-portal-copyright= " Brendan McDermid " **28;40126;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1707094 " /&gt; &lt;p&gt; There&amp;rsquo ; s been no shortage of press coverage about the link between baby powder and ovarian cancer .
Johnson &amp;amp ; Johnson has lost a string of lawsuits recently with the biggest ordering a payout of &lt;a href= " https : **33;40156;TOOLONG .
billion&lt;/a&gt; .
But the science isn&amp;rsquo ; t so clear-cut , and a new study in the &lt;a href= " https : **33;40191;TOOLONG .
of the American Medical Association&lt;/a&gt; has suggested that the risk , if it exists , is very small .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Debates about the safety of talc have been going on for over 40 years .
Talc is a mineral commonly used in cosmetic products , like talcum powder .
So when a &lt;a href= " https : **33;40226;TOOLONG .
report&lt;/a&gt; found talc particles within the tissue of ovarian and cervical cancers , people were understandably concerned .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " https : **33;40261;TOOLONG .
studies&lt;/a&gt; from the 1980s did show a link between talc and ovarian cancer and a number of subsequent studies did the same .
But more recent research from the &lt;a href= " https : **33;40296;TOOLONG .
Health Study&lt;/a&gt; , &lt;a href= " https : **33;40331;TOOLONG .
Health Initiative&lt;/a&gt; and the &lt;a href= " https : **33;40366;TOOLONG .
Study&lt;/a&gt; was actually negative .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; There are a few possible explanations for this discrepancy .
Talc , when mined , is frequently contaminated with asbestos .
In 1976 , cosmetic manufacturers permanently &lt;a href= " https : **33;40401;TOOLONG .
all asbestos&lt;/a&gt; from their products .
So one possibility is that earlier studies were seeing the cancer causing effects of asbestos , rather than talc , and the more recent studies showed no risk because products are now asbestos free .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;a href= " https : **33;40436;TOOLONG .
testing&lt;/a&gt; largely confirms that talc products are asbestos free , although a &lt;a href= " https : **33;40471;TOOLONG .
Reuter 's investigation&lt;/a&gt; and a &lt;a href= " https : **33;40506;TOOLONG .
recall&lt;/a&gt; suggest that asbestos contamination may still happen .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Another possibility for the discrepancy is recall bias .
The earlier positive studies were case-control studies .
These types of studies identify women with ovarian and then ask them about prior talcum powder use .
In effect , they work backward .
The more recent negative studies were cohort studies .
These types of studies record talcum powder use among women and then look to see if they subsequently develop ovarian cancer .
In effect , they work forward .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The danger with backward looking studies is that people with a particular disease may end up scouring their memory looking for reasons why they got sick and then over-report a particular risk factor or exposure .
The problem is made worse if they have a prior reason to believe something is dangerous .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; For example the &lt;a href= " https : **33;40541;TOOLONG .
American Cancer Epidemiology Study&lt;/a&gt; found an overall link between talc and ovarian cancer .
For women interviewed after 2014 , talcum powder nearly tripled the risk of ovarian cancer , but for women interviewed before 2014 there was no increased risk .
The year 2014 is significant because it saw a large class action lawsuit against Johnson &amp;amp ; Johnson .
The press coverage may have skewed how women remembered their prior talcum powder use , especially if they were diagnosed with ovarian cancer .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Recall bias may explain why the retrospective backward-looking case control studies were positive and the prospective forward-looking cohort studies were negative .
The problem with cohort studies is that they need a lot of patients to research rare events like ovarian cancer .
Even the recent &lt;a href= " https : **33;40576;TOOLONG .
study&lt;/a&gt; , which analyzed data on a quarter of a million women , said that it did not have enough people in it to exclude a very small increase in risk .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; But then again , why use talcum powder at all ? The &lt;a href= " https : **33;40611;TOOLONG .
Academy of Pediatrics&lt;/a&gt; actually recommends against it , not for any cancer link , but because it can be inhaled by babies and irritate lung tissue .
The &lt;a href= " https : **33;40646;TOOLONG .
College of Obstetrics and Gynecology&lt;/a&gt; is similarly unimpressed by the actual need for talcum powder for any gynecologic purpose .
So even though talc likely does not significantly increase the risk ovarian cancer , we could just stop using it altogether .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; For those who do want to keep using it , there is another solution .
They can buy baby powder made from cornstarch , because while all talcum powders are baby powders , not all baby powders contain talc .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;em&gt;Christopher Labos&lt;/em&gt; &lt;em&gt; is a Montreal doctor and an associate with the McGill Office for Science and Society .
He also co-hosts a podcast called The Body of Evidence .
&lt;/em&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;40681;TOOLONG .
&lt;ul class= " relatedlinks " &gt; &lt;li&gt;&lt;a href= " https : **33;40723;TOOLONG .
columns by Christopher **26;40758;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Christopher Labos , Special to Montreal GazetteTue , 28 Jan 2020 18:43:11 **45;40786;TOOLONG .
on fitness : Is ' load management ' really a thing in sport ? http : **34;40833;TOOLONG .
&lt;img src= " https : **33;40869;TOOLONG .
title= " The term load management became popular in the NHL and elsewhere after the Toronto Raptors claimed it as the motivation for sitting a healthy Kawhi Leonard during the regular season .
" alt= " The term load management became popular in the NHL and elsewhere after the Toronto Raptors claimed it as the motivation for sitting a healthy Kawhi Leonard during the regular season .
" data-portal-copyright= " Stan Behal " **28;40904;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1503756 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;40934;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Load management&amp;rdquo ; is one of the hottest terms in pro sports .
A regular part of the Toronto Raptors&amp;rsquo ; lexicon during last season&amp;rsquo ; s run to the NBA championships , the team claimed load management was behind their decision for sitting a healthy Kawhi Leonard during the regular season .
The term has since been picked up by the NHL , with teams using load management to keep goalies fresh over a long 82-game regular season schedule .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; The idea of managing training load isn&amp;rsquo ; t new .
It&amp;rsquo ; s been used in the endurance community for years , with runners , swimmers and triathletes establishing weekly training parameters designed to reduce the risk of injury .
Baseball pitchers are also subject to load management , with the number of pitches and starts strictly monitored by coaching staff trying to keep their athletes healthy over the course of a long season .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Yet despite the tendency for load management to be linked to injury prevention , it&amp;rsquo ; s also linked to performance .
There&amp;rsquo ; s a saying among exercise physiologists : Exposure to load allows the body to tolerate load .
In other words , the physiological adaptations triggered by training and competition are necessary to develop the fitness , strength and resilience needed to withstand the rigours of physical activity and reach peak athletic potential .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Tim Gabbett , an exercise physiologist and high-performance consultant from Australia , addressed the topic of load management in a recent &lt;a href= " https : **30;40970;TOOLONG " target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;editorial in the British Journal of Sports Medicine&lt;/a&gt; .
He suggests the concept is largely misunderstood , especially in team sports , and that many of the practices used to reduce workload are &amp;ldquo ; poorly implemented&amp;rdquo ; by coaches , trainers and medical staff .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Even the 10-per-cent rule , considered the gold standard of load management , is often misinterpreted .
Based on the theory that increases in training volume shouldn&amp;rsquo ; t exceed 10 per cent per week , Gabbett suggests it should be taken more as a recommendation than a rule because it fails to consider an athlete&amp;rsquo ; s current training load .
For anyone who is already training at the top end of their tolerance , a 10 per cent increase in volume is ill advised .
And for athletes who are undertrained , a more aggressive approach to reaching peak performance may be advised .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; For healthy athletes with clear performance goals , load management is a relatively easy task as long as the timeline to meet those goals allows for a progressive increase in training volume , intensity and/or frequency .
But for athletes who are coming back from an injury or who have a jam-packed competitive schedule , load management becomes more complex .
It&amp;rsquo ; s not easy to find that sweet spot where training load is sufficient to maximize performance , but not so aggressive that it leads to exhaustion and/or injury .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s not just the time spent training and competing that needs to be factored into load management .
Stress , travel , inadequate nutrition and lack of sleep can increase fatigue and have a negative effect on recovery .
Another important element for consideration is repetitiveness in the workload .
Athletes for whom training and competition demand the same set of movements be performed over and over again ( throwing athletes , such as pitchers , runners and swimmers ) are likely to require more stringent policies related to load management .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Then of course there is the very human factor of how tolerant the athlete is when it comes to workload .
Some athletes can endure a packed schedule of training and competition with little in the way of consequences , while others experience a dip in performance and/or a rise in injuries with a much lighter volume of work .
Some of that resilience , or lack thereof , is related to known factors such as age , history of injury , quality of sleep and speed of recovery .
But sometimes there is no easy answer for why some athletes are more or less tolerant of the same volume of work .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Establishing the appropriate &amp;lsquo ; ceiling&amp;rsquo ; of training load can , at times , be difficult for practitioners given that the demands of sport evolve over seasons and are influenced by several known contextual factors ( e .
, winning or losing , margin of victory or defeat , quality of opposition and so on ) , &amp;rdquo ; said Gabbett .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; So while there&amp;rsquo ; s no one recipe for load management , there are some basic guidelines that can be followed by amateur and elite athletes alike .
The first rule of thumb is to err on the side of moderation when it comes to training load and to minimize the degree of change from week to week .
Training load should also be in proportion to performance goals , competition schedule and degree of repetitiveness in the athlete&amp;rsquo ; s training protocols and movement patterns .
Also important is to be aware of the individual resilience of the athlete when it comes to volume of training .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; For athletes who are managing their own training schedule and for trainers and coaches who are responsible for dictating the training and competition schedules of their athletes , regular monitoring of fatigue , competitive and lifestyle-related stressors , volume of travel and injury patterns is vital to load management .
Every athlete has a point where workload goes from building tolerance and achieving peak athletic potential to being detrimental to performance .
Getting the best from the athlete without crossing that line is the key to proper load management .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h2 class= " cat-head short " **40;41002;TOOLONG .

more of Jill Barker 's Fitness columns right **25;41079;TOOLONG &lt;/ul&gt; Jill Barker , Special to Montreal GazetteSun , 26 Jan 2020 19:06:53 **45;41106;TOOLONG &amp;amp ; FitnessHealthLifeLocal NewsCoronavirus : What you need to knowhttp : **36;41153;TOOLONG .

title= " A volunteer distributes protective suits to others in Wuhan , China on February 26 , 2020 .
" alt= " A volunteer distributes protective suits to others in Wuhan , China on February 26 , 2020 .
" data-portal-copyright= " STR " **28;41226;TOOLONG " 1 " data-license-id= " 1733570 " /&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 100% " height= " 100% " frameborder= " 0 " allowfullscreen= " true " src= " https : **34;41256;TOOLONG .
&gt; &lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;p&gt; Canada&amp;rsquo ; s chief public health officer is urging Canadians to prepare for a possible outbreak of the &lt;a href= " https : **33;41292;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " **25;41327;TOOLONG .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; We can all take simple actions to protect ourselves and others from getting sick .
Washing our hands frequently , covering our coughs and sneezes &amp;mdash ; and staying home when sick , &amp;rdquo ; Dr .
Theresa Tam told reporters Thursday .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; You can prepare by having enough of your medications on hand , making a plan for the care of children or other dependents if you or someone you care for becomes ill .
Speak to your employer about alternative work arrangements and connect with your family , neighbours , community to find support .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Here&amp;rsquo ; s what you need to know .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 640 " height= " 360 " src= " https : **34;41354;TOOLONG .
frameborder= " 0 " allow= " accelerometer ; autoplay ; encrypted-media ; gyroscope ; picture-in-picture " **34;41390;TOOLONG &lt;h3&gt;What are coronaviruses ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; They are a family of viruses .
The most recently discovered one causes a coronavirus disease that has been dubbed COVID-19 .
It was first reported in Wuhan , China .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;How contagious is it ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; &amp;ldquo ; Some viruses are highly contagious ( like measles ) , while other viruses are less so , &amp;rdquo ; according to the U .
Centers for Disease Control .
&amp;ldquo ; Currently , it&amp;rsquo ; s unclear how easily or sustainably this virus is spreading between people .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;How deadly is it ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; Those who have been infected have experienced symptoms ranging from mild to severe .
&lt;a href= " https : **33;41426;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;A study published this week&lt;/a&gt; in the Journal of the American Medical Association found a mortality rate of 2 .
per cent .
The rate varied by age .
No deaths occurred in the group aged nine years and younger .
Among those 70 to 79 years old , the rate was eight per cent , and in those 80 and older , the mortality rate was 14 .
per cent .
By comparison , the seasonal flu has an overall mortality rate of about 0 .
per cent .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;Who is most at risk ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; Older people and those with chronic diseases or weakened immune systems .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;How many cases have there been ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; As of Thursday afternoon , &lt;a href= " https : **33;41461;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;it had been detected in 47 countries&lt;/a&gt; , including Canada , the World Health Organization says .
There have been more than 82,000 confirmed cases , including 2,800 deaths .
There have been no deaths in Canada .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;Are there any confirmed cases in Quebec ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; No confirmed coronavirus cases have been reported in Quebec , the health department says , but &lt;a href= " https : **33;41496;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;the province 's first suspected case was reported Thursday night&lt;/a&gt; in Montreal .
As of Thursday afternoon , &lt;a href= " https : **33;41531;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;15 people were being monitored&lt;/a&gt; in the province .
Quebec&amp;rsquo ; s public health director says &lt;a href= " https : **33;41566;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;the risk of Quebecers contracting the disease is low&lt;/a&gt; .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;What about the rest of Canada ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; There are &lt;a href= " https : **33;41601;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;13 confirmed cases in Canada&lt;/a&gt; &amp;mdash ; seven in British Columbia and six in Ontario .
The Public Health Agency of Canada says the risk associated with coronavirus is low for this country .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;iframe width= " 640 " height= " 360 " src= " https : **34;41636;TOOLONG .
frameborder= " 0 " allow= " accelerometer ; autoplay ; encrypted-media ; gyroscope ; picture-in-picture " **34;41672;TOOLONG &lt;h3&gt;What is the risk to travellers ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; It&amp;rsquo ; s &amp;ldquo ; generally low&amp;rdquo ; for Canadian travellers abroad , but it varies by country , Health Canada says .
Check the &lt;a href= " https : **33;41708;TOOLONG .
target= " blank " rel= " noopener " &gt;federal travel advisory website&lt;/a&gt; for information about individual countries .
As of Thursday , there are coronavirus travel health notices for China , Hong Kong , Iran , Japan , northern Italy , Singapore and South Korea .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;How is it diagnosed ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; A health care professional diagnoses coronavirus infections based on symptoms .
In Quebec , laboratory tests by the Laboratoire de sant&amp;eacute ; publique du Qu&amp;eacute ; bec are required to confirm the diagnosis .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;What happens if a case turns up in Quebec ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; If a case is confirmed , provincial health officials say , the risk of transmission in the community would remain low .
Health professionals &amp;ldquo ; have access to tools to quickly identify a suspected coronavirus case and to ensure it is adequately managed and rapid application of the necessary prevention and control measures , &amp;rdquo ; the provincial government says .
Public health authorities &amp;ldquo ; will immediately conduct an investigation to identify people in contact with the infected person .
&amp;rdquo ; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; If a Quebecer confirmed to have coronavirus requires hospitalization , they will be taken care of in one of four hospitals with expertise in infectious diseases .
For adults , they are the Jewish General Hospital in Montreal and the Institut universitaire de cardiologie et de pneumologie in Quebec City .
Children would be hospitalized at the Centre hospitalier universitaire Sainte-Justine in Montreal or the Centre hospitalier universitaire de l&amp;rsquo ; Universit&amp;eacute ; Laval in Quebec City .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;What are the symptoms ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; Some people show no symptoms .
Those who have coronavirus may not realize it , because symptoms can be similar to those of the flu .
People with severe cases can show symptoms associated with pneumonia .
They include fever , cough and difficulty breathing .
In rare cases , the infection can lead to death .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;How long does it take for symptoms to appear ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; Up to 14 days .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;How is the virus spread ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; The virus &amp;mdash ; which causes nose , throat and lung infections &amp;mdash ; spreads through droplets that emerge when you cough or sneeze , as well as via touching or shaking hands .
You can also contract it by touching an infected person and then touching your mouth , nose or eyes .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;How can I avoid becoming infected or spreading infection ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; Don&amp;rsquo ; t touch your eyes , nose or mouth with unwashed hands .
Wash your hands often , using soap and water for at least 20 seconds .
Stay one metre away from people who are ill .
If you&amp;rsquo ; re sick , extra precautions should be taken .
Stay home .
When you cough or sneeze , cover your mouth and nose with your arm .
After using a tissue , throw it out immediately and wash your hands .
And avoid visiting people in hospitals or long-term care centres .
&lt;/p&gt; &lt;h3&gt;How is it treated ? &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;p&gt; There is no vaccine yet .
Infected patients receive care to relieve symptoms .
Those with severe symptoms are hospitalized .
